## **Chapter 8 – A Glimpse of the Past 3**

“Alright, you’re done with your business, right? Now, get out of here!!”

The female royal guard spat the words, her voice laced with lingering anger and perhaps a hint of embarrassment.

A short time had passed after William and his wife retreated back into the bedroom, hopefully enough for the immediate tension to dissipate, but her resentment remained palpable.

“Even if you tell me to leave, this is my home in the royal capital, you know. The Salis family maintains a residence here.”

Alana retorted, her tone even.

“Ugh, don’t be so pedantic! Then go somewhere else! Or rather, just go back to the frontier already! We don’t need your kind stirring up trouble here!”

Although her voice was still loud and sharp, the royal guard’s words lacked the bite they had possessed before William’s unexpected appearance.

The nobleman’s intervention seemed to have thrown her off balance, introducing an element of uncertainty into her bravado.

“Hmm… well, since I’ve been given full authority by my father, the Margrave, perhaps you could listen to what I have to say? It concerns matters of grave importance to the kingdom.”

“Didn’t you hear me say ‘go away?!’ I have nothing to say to you people! Especially not a traitor’s daughter!”

“Now, now, why don’t we calm down first and foremost?”

Then, the male guard interjected, stepping between Alana and his agitated colleague, who looked like she was about to bite at any moment.

“Look, we’ll listen, but that doesn’t mean we can do anything about it, okay? After all, we’re just ordinary guards, following orders. Our authority is limited.”

“Hmm, that’s fine. First, just hear me out. If, after hearing me, you’re still not interested or believe me to be fabricating things, I’ll just have to take it up with the appropriate authorities myself. I’m confident they will be interested in what I have to say.”

“Hmph! Who’s going to listen to anything a traitor’s daughter says! You are wasting your time!”

The female guard let out a defiant curse still. The male guard gave a wry smile, clearly anticipating a headache.

“Hmm, speaking of ‘traitor’,” Alana said, her gaze fixed on the female guard, “wasn’t it Count Colborn who first raised suspicions that my father was planning a rebellion? The same Count Colborn who gained immensely from my father being imprisoned?”

“So what if it was? He was just doing his duty as a loyal subject to the kingdom.”

“What if that Count is involved in obvious criminal activity? What if his hands aren’t as clean as he claims? What if his sudden rise to power is built on lies?”

“What are you saying? That is treasonous talk!”

“What if his accusations are based on a personal grudge against the Salis family, or to cover up his own criminal activity? Would those accusations still be valid? Would his word still carry weight?”

Alana pressed, watching the guards closely for their reactions.

“Or do you think the King will just turn a blind eye?”

“Don’t be ridiculous–”

The male guard raised his hand, abruptly stopping his colleague’s outburst.

“Fine then, let’s hear what you have to say,” he said, his eyes conveying a weary acceptance of the situation.

“We can’t just dismiss her outright, not with the Margrave’s backing.”

Alana then proceeded to recount the events of the past few days, starting with the attack by Genber and his thugs.

She carefully began by describing the attempted assault within the Jana Forest in the past.

To substantiate her claims, she presented the guards with the same investigation documents that Yoichi had previously given to William, highlighting the inconsistencies and implicating Count Colborn.

However, she deliberately kept Amanda’s existence a secret.

The revelation of a Demon lurking within the royal capital would undoubtedly spark widespread panic and chaos, potentially jeopardizing her investigation and putting innocent lives at risk.

The less people knew, the better.

“Good heavens…”

The male guard muttered as he reviewed the documents, his face paling slightly.

“If this is true,” the female guard added, her voice uncharacteristically subdued, “then Count Colborn is lower than scum…”

“And it seems the dignitaries of the royal capital seem to be letting themselves be swayed by such a scoundrel, aren’t they?”

Alana remarked, allowing a hint of disdain to color her voice.

At Alana’s words, the female royal guard, who had been meticulously examining the documents, raised her head, her eyebrows furrowed in confusion.

“T-this could all be fabricated evidence, right? A clever deception designed to clear your father’s name!”

“That’s certainly possible,” Alana conceded, “But this time, there are witnesses. Men who confessed to the crime on their own.”

“Ugh…” The female guard groaned, holding her head in her hands.

Alana reiterated that the plan involved imprisoning and violating her after she arrived in the royal capital, painting a vivid picture of the depravity she had uncovered.

She confirmed that Kenneth and Leonard, two key figures involved in the conspiracy, were already detained, alongside Genber and his henchmen, all currently confined within the mansion.

“The thugs who tried to attack you are still alive, I presume?”

The male guard asked, his voice hardening slightly.

“Yes,” Alana replied emotionlessly.

“They weren’t worth killing. Nor were they any use if they’re dead. After all, dead men tell no tales.”

She could have easily dispatched them all, but she refused to taint her weapon with the blood of such pathetic individuals… at least, not yet.

Their value lay in their testimony, and she intended to use them to expose Count Colborn’s treachery.

“This… this information is a bit too much for us to handle,” the male guard admitted, scratching his head in frustration. “This goes way beyond our pay grade.”

“What? It’s just the concoctions of an adventurer, right? We should just ignore it! This is our duty to ignore this and get back to work!”

She was trying to remain cool, but Alana could see she was breaking a sweat.

“We can’t do that,” the male guard countered, shaking his head.

“She’s here as a representative of the Salis Margravate, and she has all this documentation and even witnesses. It would be scarier to ignore it and have problems later. We could be charged with aiding and abetting!”

“Mmph…”

The female guard grumbled, unconvinced.

Ignoring his sulking junior, the male guard held up the stack of documents Yoichi had provided.

“Would it be alright if we keep these for now? For investigation purposes, of course.”

“Yes. I have a copy, so you can have those,” Alana confirmed, signaling her assent.

“Thank you. Then, you,” the male guard said to his junior, his tone suggesting an implicit understanding.

“I’ll leave this place to you for a while. Make sure nothing happens.”

“Huh?”

The female guard exclaimed, startled by her colleague’s sudden shift in responsibility.

“I’m going to the royal castle with this. I guess I’ll ask His Excellency the Prime Minister for his judgment. This is simply beyond my authority and needs a more thorough investigation.”

“Wh-wha… Senior?”

The female guard sputtered, her face paling.

“Lady Alana, may we leave the witnesses in your care for a little while longer? We obviously don’t have the means to hold this many people.”

“Yes, fine by me.”

Alana replied, her lips curling into a faint smile.

“Then, excuse m-“

“Senior, wait!”

The female guard called out desperately to the retreating figure of the male guard, her voice laced with panic.

“…What is it?”

He asked, turning back to face her.

“Uh, well… am I going to be left alone…? With _them_?”

“Yes, that’s the plan, but is there a problem? Is the Margrave’s daughter frightening you?”

“Um, it’s not really a problem, but more like…”

The female guard glanced nervously at the bedroom door, her eyes wide with apprehension.

Fear was clearly visible on her face.

“Um, if I get “invited” again, and Senior’s not here, I might not be able to refuse…”

“Then you should just join in!”

The male guard declared, throwing his hands up.

“…Huh?”

The female guard stared blankly, completely taken aback by her senior guard’s unexpected words.

“Like the lady said earlier, those guys aren’t going to escape from here whether they’re guarded or not! So there’s no problem if you join them! You might even strike up a relationship. It will be a nice change of pace.”

“Huh? Huh?”

“Honestly, I wish I could take your place! But this information is very important and can’t be given to just anyone, you know? Telling the Prime Minister is the best thing to do for the both of us. But you can’t get the Prime Minister to take you in directly, can you?! So I have no choice but to go! If possible, I would stay and talk to that hung Margrave… Damn it! How envious I am…!!”

“No way… Senior…?”

“Anyway! I’m leaving this place to you, so you can spend your time as you like! However, I won’t allow you to leave your post. Got it!?”

Leaving those words behind, the male guard clutched the documents tightly and hurried off, leaving his junior in a state of utter bewilderment.

“Eh… wh… eeeeeh!?”

In the end, the remaining female guard could only stare in surprise and follow the retreating figure of her superior with her eyes, slumping her shoulders as soon as he disappeared from view.

“Well, now that our business here is done, let’s leave this place. As you wished,” Alana said, breaking the silence.

The female guard heard the words of the lady knight and looked up as though startled.

“W-wait…!”

“Sorry. We’re not free either. Hazel, can you take us to an empty room somewhere?”

“Yes… this way, please.”

“Don’t… don’t leave me alone…”

Alana raised a hand to stop the female guard who was trying to catch up.

“Don’t leave your post. That’s what you were ordered, right? Aren’t you sworn to protect the kingdom?”

“B-but…”

“Aren’t you a glorious royal guard? Then you should obey your superior’s orders. This isn’t your first day.”

“Ugh…”

She tried to take another step forward, but after hearing the princess knight’s words, she managed to stand still by leaning on her short spear.

“Well then, Mister Yoichi, shall we go? Hazel, please.”

“O-okay.”

“Yes, this way…”

The female guard, clinging to her short spear and staggering, collapsed to the floor and released her short spear as soon as the figures of Alana and the others disappeared from view.

The short spear rolled across the floor with a dry clang.

— Click… Squeak…

And as if waiting for the timing, the bedroom door opened.

---

Yoichi and the others found themselves in a generously sized room within the mansion.

While it didn’t quite reach the opulent heights of William’s bedroom, with its private en-suite bathing facilities, it was certainly comfortable.

There was bed large enough to accommodate four or five adults dominated the space, and the room was plentifully furnished with tables, chairs, and plush sofas – enough seating for a group of ten to relax comfortably.

After designating this room as their Home Point for convenient returns, Yoichi [Returned] to “Grand Court 2503,” his apartment unit in Japan.

There, he gathered Karin, Misato, and Xihan, bringing them back with him to the mansion.

He’d intentionally kept them waiting in Japan, rather than the other world, primarily because he knew he could contact them from basically any location over there.

On a quick detour, he also dropped by the Smiths’ Workshop in Meilgrad, hoping to include Samantha in their gathering.

However, Samantha politely declined, explaining that she was immersed in a particularly demanding project.

It seemed that she possessed little interest in the intricacies of other people’s family matters, always eager to work on her crafts.

Besides, as the esteemed alchemical blacksmith of the frontier, she was perpetually engrossed in one task or another, keeping her schedule perpetually full.

“Um, is that royal guard girl gonna be okay, though?”

Karin asked, her voice laced with concern.

After listening to Yoichi and Alana’s explanation of the situation so far, these were the first words out of her mouth, revealing her immediate worry for the young woman’s well-being.

“Ah, I was wondering about that too, actually.”

Misato chimed in, echoing Karin’s sentiments.

She was looking at Alana expectantly, waiting for reassurance.

Here, Alana reassured them.

“Don’t worry. Father isn’t the kind of man to force himself on someone against their will. He values consent and wouldn’t take advantage of anyone.”

“So, if the girl really objects, it’ll be fine, right? He wouldn’t ignore her wishes?”

Misato pressed, wanting to be absolutely sure.

“Yes, of course. But…”

Alana nodded in response to Misato’s question, offering a comforting affirmation.

However, a shadow of seriousness quickly crossed her face, hinting at a more complex situation.

“Is there a problem?”

Yoichi inquired, sensing the shift in Alana’s demeanor.

He wanted to understand the full scope of the potential complications.

“Well, there’s the matter of the legal wife”

“The legal wife? You mean that blonde lady? The one we glimpsed earlier?”

Yoichi asked, trying to connect the pieces.

His mind conjured an image of the elegant woman in the bathrobe with the radiant blonde hair he had caught a glimpse of earlier.

“Yes. Her name is Isabel. She is my father’s legal wife, and holds significant sway within the family,” Alana confirmed, elaborating on Isabel’s position.

Yoichi recalled hearing before that Alana had several older sisters, and that William practiced polygamy with multiple wives.

However, this was the first time he’d met any other than Hortense, adding a new layer of complexity to his understanding of William’s family dynamics.

The other two women he’d briefly encountered in the mansion must have been concubines, holding a different status than a wife.

“Will something happen if she’s around? Is she likely to interfere?”

Karin asked, her worry palpable.

“Well, she’s very charming, and a very skilled speaker, you see. She has a way with words and can often influence those around her.”

“Could it be that he gets easily manipulated by his wife? That he’s susceptible to her influence?”

Misato also speculated, trying to understand the potential dynamic between William and Isabel.

“I can’t say that’s impossible. After all, it seems that my mother and father’s marriage was largely thanks to her assistance… Isabel played a key role in bringing them together.”

Alana revealed at the end, hinting at the depth of Isabel’s involvement in William’s life and the subtle power she wielded.

---

Hortense was born just as Meilgrad transitioned from a rough-and-tumble frontier settlement to something resembling an actual town.

At that time, the days of raw, untamed wilderness were slowly receding, little by little being replaced by the burgeoning infrastructure of a developing community.

That’s why her developing years were spent immersed in the culture of the pioneers and adventurers who flocked to the burgeoning town, men and women who carved a life out of the wilderness.

This upbringing fostered in her a refreshingly liberated attitude toward matters of intimacy, especially with regards to the opposite sex.

Of course, as a parent, Celestin was largely uncomfortable with it, yet found himself largely unable to control her whims.

Attempts at imposing restrictions were always met with Francois’ sharp retort: “That child doesn’t have someone special like _you_ for me, so please be lenient on her.”

Celestin, it seemed, had long since learned that certain battles were not worth fighting, and so he tacitly approved, or at least tolerated, her daughter’s choices.

Consequently, during her early years, Hortense lived a vibrant life.

She actively participated in the dangers and excitements of adventuring, proving herself a capable warrior in her own right.

And, in addition to her professional pursuits, she indulged in what could be described as “sampling” the local masculine talent, showing a distinct preference for muscular, well-built men.

This was, of course, before a formal lord established his presence in Meilgrad.

Years later, William, the future heir to the lordship, was born.

As William grew into a young man, he developed a powerful admiration, bordering on infatuation, for Hortense during his adolescence.

She embodied the spirit of Meilgrad – strong, independent, and undeniably attractive.

But William’s admiration wasn’t unique.

Celestin, François, and Hortense, the trio of pioneering figures, were the subject of widespread admiration within Meilgrad.

Nearly every resident had, at some point, held one or all of them in high esteem.

They were symbols of the town’s hard-won progress and its indomitable spirit.

William, aware of his destiny to become the next lord, dedicated himself to preparing for the role since childhood.

He diligently cultivated his talents, honed his abilities, and amassed political power.

His efforts instilled in him a strong sense of self-assurance, a confidence that he could achieve anything he set his mind to.

And with that confidence, he decided to pursue Hortense’s affections.

“I’m sorry, William, but I don’t particularly care for whippersnappers like you,” was her blunt and dismissive reply.

William was, understandably, shocked.

This was a man accustomed to getting what he wanted.

But he was nothing if not persistent. He had no intention of giving up.

He resolved to understand what made Hortense tick, to discover the qualities that attracted her.

He embarked on a thorough investigation into the preferences and past “samples” the object of his affection had “eaten” so far.

“My mother,” Alana relayed to Yoichi, “well, she seems to have a predilection for muscular men.”

“Your dad’s incredibly macho… but wasn’t he like that when he was young?”

“Yes. I’ve seen portraits of him from his teenage years. Apart from the hair and eye color, his general appearance was very similar to Henry’s.”

“Seriously…”

Yoichi muttered, picturing the young man with blue hair he had only met once.

Henry possessed a slender, almost superstar-like appeal, a far cry from Yoichi’s image of the younger William.

“After that,” Alana continued, “Father apparently started working out like crazy. He was already a strong man, but he then took his fitness to another level.”

He switched from a saber, a weapon that prioritized speed and skill, to a heavy two-handed battle axe, a tool that demanded raw strength and endurance.

He actively participated in the ongoing forest development projects and relentlessly hunted monsters that threatened the town.

He was desperate to gain Hortense’s attention, but his efforts had an unexpected, and beneficial, side effect: he solidified his reputation and gained the respect of the adventurer community.

It took nearly a decade of relentless self-improvement before he finally met Hortense’s exacting standards, which started when he was in his late teens.

“By this time, Father was already married, and my sisters had been born.”

As the son of a noble family, and the eldest son of a high-ranking noble like a frontier count, William’s choice of a partner couldn’t be based solely on romantic desires.

Political considerations, familial alliances, and the need to secure an heir all played a role.

Isabel, whom Yoichi had previously met, had been chosen as his legal wife, and there were, in addition, two more concubines within the household.

“So, Hortense was okay with that kind of arrangement?”

“Yes. In fact, my mother actually seemed to prefer men who were already married with children.”

This wasn’t necessarily driven by a desire to seduce or to steal men away from their families.

Rather, it stemmed from Hortense’s pragmatic outlook.

She sought relationships that were less likely to result in complications, messy breakups, or unwanted drama.

Although, of course, the messy aftermath and rumors could hardly be avoided if revealed.

It was her reasoning that if a man was already married with children, he would be less inclined to openly boast about his affair, less likely to jeopardize his existing family structure.

She also had to consider the role of the women in their lives.

Furthermore, the societal norms of Meilgrad, at least, seemed to exhibit a certain tolerance, or perhaps resignation, toward husbands engaging in extramarital affairs, regardless of whether their partners were amateurs or sex workers.

The husbands, in turn, often seemed to tacitly acknowledge the possibility that their wives might be seeking companionship elsewhere, but rarely pursued the matter with any real vigor.

Yoichi reflected on this information.

“When it comes to sexual or romantic ethics, there can be considerable differences depending on the region, era, and culture. This was also true in my original world, so it would be pointless to judge them based on Japanese common sense.”

(Well, I’m not really in a position to say anything…)

Yoichi’s own romantic life was anything but simple.

He had ongoing relationships with Alana, Karin, Misato, Xihan, and even Samantha, despite her physical absence.

And that wasn’t the extent of it.

He still occasionally met with Charlotte, the former intelligence agent, and their encounters sometimes led to shared intimacy.

He had also shared a bed with the members of The “Red Flash” – Myna, Jessica, and Greta – for a brief period.

Beyond that, he had enjoyed a one-night stand with Donna, a female investigator he had partnered with in the casino city, and prior to that, he had frequently engaged the services of Sayaka, also known as Lina, a sex worker, in private.

If the wrong kind of activist were to discover the intricacies of his personal life, he would be condemned without reservation.

Yoichi, at least, recognized that he wasn’t in a position to pass judgment on the relationship choices of others.

Plus, there was the sensitive issue of Misato’s traumatic past with his brother, who had exploited her feelings and treated her as a plaything.

Given the nature of their current relationship, it would be deeply hurtful and hypocritical for him to raise objections to others’ behavior now.

“Apparently, my mother never intended to marry my father in the first place. My father had mostly resigned himself to that fact, too.”

Alana resumed her explanation, a hint of amusement lacing her words.

William, a man who held a deep admiration for beautiful and strong women, had eventually taken three wives and fathered children with them.

Consequently, the initial intensity of his obsession with Hortense had waned considerably.

He had come to terms with the situation, at least outwardly.

Of course, she was the woman he yearned for in his youth, the woman who had, in many ways, reshaped his very way of life.

A part of him still desired to have her as his wife, if such a thing were possible. He cherished her deeply.

That’s what he thought, at least.

He couldn’t bring himself to be forceful, to try and wrest away his first love’s freedom, a freedom he knew she always guarded fiercely.

He respected her too much for that.

Besides, she wasn’t someone he could simply subdue by force, even if he were inclined to do so.

Hortense possessed a strength, both physical and mental, that rivaled his own.

On the other hand, for Hortense, William was but one of many partners, albeit a significant one.

Their relationship was one of convenience, a dance of mutual benefit and respect that blossomed into a deep friendship.

They engaged in intimate relations and shared experiences only when it was mutually desirable and suitable for each other’s lives — a complex, unconventional relationship if one would describe it.

“In the midst of all this intricate interplay, Isabel made a move.”

Alana continued, a knowing glint showing in her eyes.

Isabel, a woman of considerable grace and charm, had married William and hailed from a respectable count’s family.

Despite her high-ranking noble lineage, she possessed a disarming humility and genuine friendliness that endeared her to many.

She never flaunted her status and treated everyone with respect.

Originally, in Meilgrad, there existed a noticeable separation between the adventurers’ guild and the margrave’s standing army.

It wasn’t a matter of animosity, but rather a lack of active engagement and collaboration between the two factions.

When William, driven by his admiration for Hortense and the adventuring spirit, began working alongside adventurers, the adventurers’ goodwill towards the lord’s family increased considerably.

This collaboration greatly improved relations between the two factions, but it still didn’t immediately lead to a closer relationship with the standing army.

It is said that it was Lady Isabel who masterfully bridged that gap between the two distinct groups.

With her radiant beauty and generous, friendly personality, a rare and cherished quality in the frontier, she quickly became beloved by many, not just within the nobility but among the common folk as well.

She was already highly regarded by the soldiers under William’s command.

As William began spending more time working with adventurers, Isabel occasionally visited the guild, gradually becoming known and soon achieving widespread popularity.

With Isabel positioned in the middle, the adventurers and the army were able to naturally close the distance, fostering a sense of camaraderie and unified purpose.

They even began conducting joint training exercises regularly.

It was even said that Meilgrad’s overall defense capabilities had effectively doubled as a direct result of this increased cooperation and mutual understanding.

“My mother told me that apparently she had a man in the past whom she wished to spend her life with.”

However, that man tragically lost his life in a fierce battle with monsters while working to develop the frontier, a common fate among the early pioneers.

Yet, even if he had survived, even if they had spent their lives together in blissful union, the inevitable difference in their lifespans would have cast a long shadow.

Hortense, as a long-lived dark elf, would have been left alone to mourn his passing when that human man reached the natural end of his lifespan.

“After realizing that stark reality, my mother began to consciously avoid getting deeply involved with any particular person.”

The pain of inevitable loss was a burden her mother chose to avoid.

Isabel, being a frequent visitor to the Adventurer’s Guild alongside William, naturally became good friends with Hortense.

Their bond was genuine and based on mutual respect and admiration.

And one day, amidst their close friendship, she subtly inquired and eventually learned that her husband, William, harbored a relationship with Hortense — a fact that could have sparked jealousy and ruined everything.

But instead this became a catalyst for change that even strenghted the connection between the two.

_“If little Isabel hadn’t been there, I probably wouldn’t have married your Papa,”_ Alana remembers her mother saying wistfully, her voice tinged with a mixture of gratitude and a sense of inevitability.

Isabel’s presence had been the key to unlocking a future Hortense had never dared to imagine.

Alana had later become an adventurer herself, joining the same guild where her parents’ stories were whispered in hushed tones.

Meaning she would eventually hear snippets of her mother’s past in the form of rumors and gossip.

She admitted that she didn’t initially feel very good upon hearing that her mother had been in relationships with numerous men before marrying her father.

She was even quite shocked and taken aback when she directly asked her mother about it and was met with an honest confirmation.

However, she knew that her father, William, had also openly taken multiple women as wives, and having grown up in the same place as her mother, she had a rough understanding that the women in Meilgrad were generally more open-minded about matters of sexuality and relationships.

Therefore, she didn’t go so far as to harbor any significant dislike or resentment toward her mother.

Nevertheless, she subconsciously avoided topics related to men and women in her personal life as a result of these early revelations.

(Is it thanks to Mister Yoichi, I wonder?)

Alana pondered, a thoughtful expression crossing her face.

Perhaps Yoichi’s presence had helped her navigate these complex feelings.

It was only after she met Yoichi and began to confide in him that Alana truly heard the full story of how her mother and father had ultimately come together.

And to be honest, she admitted to feeling a little put off by the blunt and straightforward manner in which the story was told…

As an aside, the reason Alana’s virginity had remained protected until she met Yoichi was largely due to the overprotective nature of Celestin.

Her grandfather, who doted on his grandchildren to the point of foolishness, had been diligently eliminating any “bad bugs” that might be crawling around his beloved granddaughter, ensuring that only the most worthy suitor would ever have a chance.

“So, how exactly did Isabel persuade Hortense to marry your father?”

Yoichi asked, his curiosity piqued.

“Who knows? It seems to be their little secret.”

Along with that coy remark, Alana smiled slightly, leaving the mystery of Isabel’s persuasive powers tantalizingly unanswered.

---

“Um, I know it’s bad form to say this after hearing such a compelling story, but why were we even discussing all this in the first place?”

The tale of William and his complex relationships had been captivating, but the initial reason for their conversation seemed to have faded.

“It’s because of the Royal Guard woman, wasn’t it? The one we left on duty in front of the bedroom,” Karin reminded the bewildered Yoichi, snapping her fingers.

“Oh, that’s right!”

Yoichi exclaimed, his memory jogged.

He recalled the somber expression on the face of the female guard of the royal palace.

From what he could gather, the guard harbored feelings, perhaps even a deep affection, for the stoic senior male guard.

However, the man seemed utterly oblivious, or perhaps simply uninterested, in her affections.

Before they’d slipped away, she looked as if she’d been struck by a cruel and undeniable truth.

Yoichi mused, _If Isabel were here, she could probably take advantage of a situation like that with her silver tongue and turn the tables on everyone involved…_

“Well, it’s not our business, I guess?” but he eventually concluded, a touch of nonchalance in his voice.

In response, everyone around him offered a wry smile, a shrug of their shoulders, or a nod of agreement, tacitly acknowledging the truth of his statement.

Just as they thought the conversation was drawing to a close, Karin tentatively raised her hand, a mischievous glint in her eye.

“Um, Alana? Can I ask just one last thing?”

“Go ahead, Karin,” Alana replied, hiding her amusement behind a smile.

“Is William, like… into men too?”

Karin blurted out, her question hanging in the air.

“Hey, Karin.”

Yoichi immediately interjected, a hint of embarrassment coloring his cheeks at the audacity of the question.

However, Misato and Xihan, their curiosity piqued, turned their expectant gazes towards Alana, eager to hear her response.

Alana chuckled softly, a playful smile gracing her lips.

“Hehe… I wonder. I don’t remember hearing anything like that…” she answered, adding a mysterious shrug for added effect.

As they were enjoying their leisurely conversation, the tranquility of the room was shattered by a sudden commotion coming from outside.

“Please wait, Master! You cannot barge in like this!” a voice pleaded.

“Get out of my way! I must see my sister!” another voice roared, filled with an anger barely contained.

“That I cannot do! Lady Alana has only just arrived, and such an intrusion would be highly disrespectful!”

“Shut up! Get out of my way, I said!!”

“Kyaah…!”

A sharp, startled cry pierced through the escalating argument.

After a brief but intense struggle, punctuated by the sounds of scuffling and protest, the door to the room was thrown open with a violent crash, splintering the surrounding wood.

Standing in the shattered doorway, his eyes bloodshot and wild, stood Henry, his face contorted with a desperate plea.

“Sister! You came here to see me, didn’t you?!”

+++

## **Chapter 9 – The Master-Servant Relationship between Henry and Hazel**

The members of TOKOROTEN didn’t seem particularly surprised by Henry’s abrupt intrusion.

In fact, they already knew Henry had returned, and that he had rushed in after Hazel informed him of Alana’s visit, thanks to Yoichi’s [Appraisal+] skill.

“Sister… to come all this way from the frontier, just to see me…”

Henry, his bloodshot eyeballs trembling minutely, staggered closer.

His words were laced with a mix of excitement and desperation, as if he was eager to reconnect with his sister.

Meanwhile, Alana, who was already standing up from the sofa, walked toward Henry’s direction.

She only stopped when she was directly in front of her brother, her expression unreadable.

“Ah… Sister… as expected, you are as beautiful as ever.”

Henry immediately offered a somewhat subservient smile. But the princess knight only cast a cold gaze at her brother, her eyes narrowing slightly as she scanned his appearance.

“Henry, I did not come to see you. I came to see Father’s condition.”

With a firm and controlled voice, she continued.

“It has been several days since I heard what happened and came here, but why has Father not yet been freed? As the next head of the Salis family, what exactly have you been doing, Henry?”

Upon learning that his sister had come to see their father, not him, Henry’s expression clouded over.

His face fell, and he looked crestfallen, as if he had been expecting a different reaction from Alana.

But when asked what he had been doing as the _next head of the Salis family_, that same face of his unusually brightened.

“Listen, Sister! I worked hard for the Salis family! In fact, I discussed it with Lord Patrick and have secured the future of the house already!!”

It was a voice filled with a sense of pride and accomplishment, as if exclaiming something one could be proud of.

However, his words were met with skepticism by Alana.

“Oh, I see… then why has Father not been freed?”

She asked, raising an eyebrow to his brother.

To this, Henry’s expression faltered, and he hesitated before responding.

“L-listen sister. I-It’s because Father was plotting a rebellion! He must be judged properly!! Normally, the Salis family could have been wiped out from this alone! But I asked Lord Patrick, and he took measures to ensure the Salis family’s continuation!!”

The voice of the younger half-brother was laced with a mix of defensiveness and desperation.

“Henry!?”

This time, voice filled with concern and surprise upon hearing her master’s words was heard.

This belonged to none other than Hazel’s, who was thinking he had said the same thing just the other day, only to change his mind halfway.

At first, she thought about it as a result of the nervousness of her father being tried in court.

But upon discovering he had reverted back to his previous stance, Hazel couldn’t help but feel a sense of disappointment and frustration.

_As if every time he went to Patrick, master becomes strange_.

Hazel, gripped by the fear of such thought, tried to make sense of the situation.

“N-no, it’s not like that, Lady Alana! Henry, Henry was…”

She tried to interject.

But Alana stopped her with a raised hand and nodded broadly.

Alana’s expression was unreadable, but thankfully, her eyes seemed to hold a deep understanding of the situation.

“Ah… uuu…”

Seeing her mistress in such state, Hazel felt a strange sense of relief wash over her, as if she had finally found someone who understood the complexity of the situation.

“That’s right! Sister, let’s go to Lord Patrick’s place too! He was also eager to see you! If I bring sis to him, he’ll surely be pleased…”

Henry spoke again, this time full of excitement and anticipation.

However, this was met with a mixture of confusion and concern by Alana, who seemed to be trying to make sense of her brother’s actions.

Yet, as if completely oblivious to the exchange between Alana and Hazel, Henry continued his speech with unfocused eyes, not removing his gaze from his older sibling.

His words were laced with a sense of desperation, as if he was trying to convince himself that he was doing the right thing.

“Leave the rest to Lord Patrick, and from now on, I’ll live with you, sis! Come on, sis, with me—”

—_Slap!_

However, before he could finish his sentence, a dry sound echoed in the room,

“—Eh…?”

Which was followed by Henry’s stunned expression, his eyes wide with shock and confusion.

“Eh… what, why…”

Clutching his stinging cheek and looking back, he finally realized that he had been slapped on his cheeks.

By none other than her beloved elder sister.

“Pathetic… Even as my brother, that was pathetic of you, Henry.”

Her voice firm and authoritative, the princess knight’s face was set in a stern expression, her eyes blazing with anger and disappointment.

“Ah… Sis…ter…?”

Meanwhile, Henry’s face contorted in a mix of pain and shock, his eyes welling up with tears as he stumbled backward.

Seeing his sibling still trying his best to process what just happened, Alana’s expression didn’t change, but her voice took on a slightly harsher tone.

“What do you mean, ‘asking Lord Patrick’! Listen, Henry! The Salis family won their autonomy and noble title in the frontier with their own hands!! It was not something given by asking someone!! If that status is unjustly lowered, you must resist! If your rights are unjustly taken, you must take them back!!”

Henry’s face scrunched up in confusion, his eyes darting back and forth as he tried to make sense of Alana’s words.

“B-but, if it continues like this, the Salis family will… And the Colborn family is the main lineage…”

He said, his voice laced with a sense of fear and uncertainty. Alana’s expression turned stern once again, her eyes blazing with anger and frustration.

“What of it!! Whoever tries to take our status and rights is our enemy, no matter who they are!! Shouldn’t you be fighting them!? Yet you, without even lifting your sword, dared to wag your tail at the enemy…” she exclaimed, her voice firm and authoritative.

Henry’s face fell, his eyes welling up with tears as he stumbled backward, his body language screaming nothing but defeat.

Having said that much, Alana let out a big sigh, her chest heaving with emotion.

“In any case… I hate weaklings and cowards like you…”

Alana’s voice was firm and controlled.

Yet, from this alone, Henry’s expression vanished, his mouth hanging open, frozen in shock and pain.

Soon after, his eyebrows drooped, and his lips began to tremble.

“Sister… hates… me…?”

He whispered, his voice barely audible.

Alana’s expression remained the same, but her voice took on a slightly softer tone.

“Yes. I hate you,” she ended, her words hanging in the air like a challenge.

“Why, are you, like that… I… worked hard for the Salis family… I even asked Lord Patrick…”

Alana’s expression turned stern once again, her eyes blazing with anger and frustration.

“That’s why I’m telling you that you’re doing it wrong! If you are a man of the Salis family, why don’t you bring me Patrick’s head?”

“Lord Patrick’s… head…? Defy Lord Patrick…? Ugh…”

“Henry…?”

Henry, who had been standing there in a daze, suddenly clutched his head, crouched down, and began to groan.

“No, no, no… I can’t defy Lord Patrick… But if I don’t, Sister will hate me… Ahhhhh!!”

He exclaimed, his voice laced with a sense of despair like never before.

Just then, Yoichi stopped Alana, who was about to approach her crouching sibling.

“Alana, didn’t I tell you? Henry is under a charm spell.”

Alana’s expression turned skeptical, her eyes narrowing slightly as she took in Yoichi’s words.

“But, Mister Yoichi…”

“It’s not something he can overcome with willpower… but wait, maybe it’s starting to wear off a little?” Yoichi said, his eyes fixed intently on Henry.

“R-really…?”

While calming the flustered Alana, Yoichi observed Henry, his eyes fixed intently on the young man.

“Yo…ichi…?”

At that moment, Henry, who had been crouching, raised his head and caught sight of Yoichi.

“Yoichi… YOICHIIIIIII! It’s all your fault…!!”

With wide, glaring eyes, Henry glared at Yoichi and shouted, his body language screaming nothing but full aggression.

“You, because of you, everything went into disarray! My sister, my father, the frontier, they’ve all gone crazy after you came!!”

Henry tried to stand up as if he was about to pounce, but perhaps his legs couldn’t support him, he stumbled and fell to his knees.

“Sister… Sister said she hated me for being weak… Does that mean she likes strong men…?”

“…Ah, yes. I like strong people.”

Alana, taken aback by the sudden question, answered hesitantly.

“Then… Then why are you with him?! What are you doing with a guy that looks nothing but weak!?”

Seeing her brother, who had tears streaming down his face and was spitting as he pleaded, Alana wore a slightly bewildered expression.

After shaking her head a few times, she looked at her brother intently and spoke.

“Mister Yoichi is strong.”

Henry’s face scrunched up in confusion, His mouth opening and closing a few times before clenching his teeth.

“Liar… Liar, liar, LIAR, LIAR, LIAR!! There’s no way he’s strong…! No way someone like this… is strong…” he started exclaiming, his crazy thoughts transforming into a full-blown wrath.

Then, whether it was willpower or some other reason, Henry, who successfully stood up despite his hypnotic state, glared at Yoichi and pointed.

“It’s a duel!! Yoichi! Duel me!!”

“Ah, sure. Let’s do it.”

and Yoichi readily accepted Henry’s proposal, his expression calm and unchanged.

---

“I’m sorry about this, Mister Yoichi…”

Alana’s voice resounded in a low volume as the group made their way toward the training grounds in the mansion’s courtyard.

The afternoon sun cast long shadows across the manicured lawn, a stark contrast to the tension that hung thick in the air.

Recalling the events that had precipitated this impromptu duel, Alana bowed her head, a mixture of guilt and embarrassment washing over her.

She never intended for things to escalate like this.

Seeing her like this, Yoichi chuckled, a low rumble in his chest.

“Don’t worry about it, Alana. Think of it as… charity work for your cute little brother.”

Yoichi’s reason for accepting Henry’s challenge wasn’t solely altruistic, nor solely for Alana’s sake.

He was playing a longer game, a delicate dance of observation and manipulation.

Earlier, he had felt a subtle shift in the air, that is, a faint crack in the magical edifice that bound Henry.

Yes. When Alana had reprimanded Henry earlier, her disgust plain on her face, the charm spell clinging to Henry had demonstrably weakened.

It was a fragile thing, this magic, dependent on emotional resonance.

“He must have been quite shocked by Alana hating him, even momentarily,” Yoichi mused, more to himself than anyone else.

He watched Alana, gauging her reaction.

“Hmm… Is that so? Even if you say that, I honestly don’t know what I should do…” Alana confessed, her brow furrowed in concern.

For Alana, Henry was, first and foremost, her brother.

That’s why the shift in his affections, the intensity in his gaze, was alien and unsettling to her.

Alana had never considered his brother in a romantic light.

However, seeing Henry’s raw emotion, that potent mix of longing and dependency, made it abundantly clear that his feelings extended far beyond simple sibling love.

To be brutally honest, she couldn’t comprehend it, nor did she feel the slightest inclination to reciprocate.

While she could easily dismiss the advances of a stranger, she couldn’t simply abandon her own blood relative.

She felt trapped, unsure how to navigate this treacherous territory.

“Well, leave that to me. I have a… plan, sort of,” Yoichi said, a glint in his eye.

He didn’t intend to spout some cliché about “men understanding each other through fighting,” although there was a grain of truth to it.

Rather, he understood the potential of a carefully orchestrated shock to disrupt the charm’s hold of his mind.

He knew that a mental and physical blow was highly likely to further destabilize the enchantment.

However, while he couldn’t be absolutely certain, even with the analytical capabilities of [Appraisal+], and factoring in the unpredictable nature of human emotions, he reasoned that a decisive defeat at Yoichi’s hands would weaken the charm even further.

If everything went according to plan, it might even be completely dispelled, freeing Henry from its insidious influence.

_(Well, forgive me if it doesn’t go well. It’s worth a shot, at any rate.)_

Yoichi had somewhat resigned himself to the possibility that his theory might be flawed, that the charm might prove more resilient than he anticipated.

After all, Henry, in his current charmed state, was little more than a persistent nuisance.

If he could eliminate that annoyance and, simultaneously, alleviate some of Alana’s considerable psychological burden, he considered it a worthwhile endeavor.

With that thought firmly in mind, he had accepted Henry’s impulsive challenge.

“What weapon?”

Henry asked, turning Yoichi’s attention to the matter at hand.

“A dagger. A single-edged one if possible,” and Yoichi answered, preferring the familiar weight and balance of such a blade.

“Hmph…”

Henry’s expression in return was a mixture of defiance and nervous anticipation.

He stalked over to the weapons rack, a haphazard assortment of training swords, blunted axes, and practice spears.

There, he selected a single-edged dagger, its steel gleaming dully in the afternoon light, and threw it, perhaps a bit too forcefully, towards Yoichi.

Compared to the lovesick puppy he’d been only moments ago, Henry now appeared much more focused, his movements more deliberate, his gaze sharper and composed.

“It’s good to see your recovery went well,” Yoichi remarked, catching the dagger with ease.

It was apparent that a duel wouldn’t be possible with Henry in such a distraught state, so Misato had stepped in, employing her restorative magic to mend his wounds and calm his frayed nerves.

As a bonus, Yoichi’s specially prepared blood capsule had also been forcibly administered.

His bodily fluids, imbued with the properties of [Healthy Body αAlpha], possessed potent restorative effects, not only replenishing stamina and magic power but also accelerating recovery from abnormal status conditions.

“Huh, I do feel a bit refreshed, actually,” Henry admitted, flexing his fingers.

The manic gleam in his eyes seemed to have diminished.

_Yeah, that’s because the charm weakened even further, thanks to that little cocktail,_ Yoichi explained, but only in his mind.

The Demon’s charm, already weakened by the shock of Alana’s rejection and the initial disruption caused by her harsh words, was now further undermined by the subtle but significant enhancement of [Healthy Body αAlpha].

Henry was slowly, almost imperceptibly, regaining his true self.

That is, until the tension was momentarily broken as the assembled women began to offer their… unique brand of support to Yoichi.

“Hey, I have an idea. Why don’t you just “do it” with Henry, Yoichi?”

“No, Karin! What are you even talking about?”

“That’s right! If we inject Yoichi’s “essence” into that brat’s system and flood it well, even something like a demon’s charm would be a one-shot deal!”

“I’m absolutely _not_ doing that, Xihan! What the _fuck_!?”

“Ah, maybe he’ll also get[Healthy Body βBeta]?”

“Misato, what are you saying too!?”

“Mmm… As his sister, I feel a bit… complicated about the idea of being _netonare-d_ by my own brother, but if I consider it part of the _treatment_…”

“I told you all, I’m _not_ doing it! And where did you even learn that word, Alana!?”

“What are you doing! Hurry up and get ready for the fight already!!”

Henry’s patience finally snapped at the women chatting freely.

“Oops, sorry,” Yoichi also turned and faced Henry with an apologetic shrug. Though he also shot a look at the women, his expression conveying a mix of amusement and mild exasperation, as if to say, “I got told off, didn’t I?”

Karin simply put her hands together, winked suggestively, and stuck out her tongue playfully.

Xihan gave Yoichi a sly, knowing smile, while Misato looked away, whistling a clumsy, off-key tune.

Alana smiled in exasperation, shrugged her shoulders, then her expression grew serious and she nodded solemnly.

It seemed she was entrusting Henry’s well-being to him, placing her faith in his ability to resolve this mess.

“If I win, you are to never appear before my sister again,” Henry declared, his voice firm.

He brandished the saber in his right hand and gripped the dagger tightly in his left, his knuckles white.

Hazel, her face etched with worry, watched nervously from a few meters behind him, her hand hovering near his back as if she wanted to offer comfort but didn’t dare.

“Then what happens if _I_ win?”

Yoichi countered, his tone deceptively light.

“What?”

Henry blinked, taken aback by the question. He hadn’t considered the possibility of his own defeat.

“Not being able to see Alana is… incredibly difficult for me. Honestly, it’s more painful than dying,” Yoichi added, allowing a hint of genuine emotion to color his voice.

“Mister Yoichi…”

Alana’s cheeks flushed pink at Yoichi’s declaration, and the other women nudged at her playfully with their elbows and fingers, teasing her about his obvious affection.

Seeing the women, including his own sister, acting so flirty and lighthearted towards Yoichi, Henry gritted his teeth, his frustration mounting.

“To have so many women at your beck and call, to be so brazenly… desired…” Henry sputtered, searching for the right words to express his resentment.

“Is that a problem? For me, they are all precious people. I can’t imagine losing even one of them,” Yoichi replied, his gaze sweeping over the assembled women, a genuine warmth in his eyes.

At his words, several of the women blushed bashfully and glanced at each other, a shared feeling of affection and camaraderie passing between them.

That display of affection, in turn, seemed to further infuriate Henry, fueling his determination to win.

“Then I’ll do whatever you say! If you tell me to die, I’ll die!” Henry shouted, his voice trembling with emotion.

“Is that so… Then…”

A mischievous smile slowly spread across Yoichi’s face, hinting at the playful, unpredictable nature that lay beneath his calm exterior.

“If you lose, how about you call me ‘brother-in-law’?”

He suggested, his eyes twinkling with amusement.

“Don’t mess with me—!!”

Fuelled by a potent mix of anger and resentment towards Yoichi’s casual demeanor, Henry exploded into motion.

He charged forward, his saber whistling through the air in a downward arc.

The strike possessed the crispness and precision honed through rigorous training under Vista, a testament to the butler’s demanding tutelage.

“Whoa there, simmer down!”

Naturally, on the other side, Yoichi was shocked.

But to this initial, arguably a surprise attack, he deftly evaded the blade, narrowly missing its mark.

Then, with a fluid shift in position, he increased the distance between them, creating a buffer zone.

“Hold your horses, Henry. We haven’t even established the ground rules yet. What constitutes a win, or a loss, for that matter?”

“Until one of us surrenders… or dies! That’s the only rule you need to know!”

Henry roared back, his voice laced with animosity as he did another lunge.

But Yoichi, displaying remarkable agility, sidestepped Henry’s renewed advance and retreated further.

He maintained a composed expression in stark contrast to Henry’s fiery rage.

“Let’s define the parameters _before_ you try to skewer me, shall we? It’s only fair.”

“Shut up! Once I’ve eliminated you, everything will be set right in this house! Everything will be fine! If only you weren’t here, meddling in my affairs…”

Henry spat out, his words a torrent of pent-up frustration.

“Whopsie-daisy,” Yoichi said with a hint of amusement.

Evading yet another reckless advance, he swiftly closed the distance to Hazel, positioning himself directly beside her.

His movements were smooth and unhurried, a stark contrast to Henry’s frantic aggression.

“Then our Hazel shall be the referee this time, it only makes sense if it’s her.”

“What!?”

Henry blurted out, his face contorted in disbelief.

“Huh?”

Hazel gasped, her eyes widening in surprise.

At this unexpected proposition, Henry’s aggressive movements faltered, his momentum visibly broken.

He stood frozen, his anger momentarily checked by the sheer absurdity of the situation.

“Because I have no intention of actually harming you, Henry. But if you refuse to yield, this charade could drag on indefinitely, right? So, if Hazel deems the fight concluded, it’s over. A fair compromise, wouldn’t you agree at least?”

Yoichi explained calmly.

A tense silence hung in the air as Henry considered the proposition.

Finally, he relented with a grudging nod.

“…Fine. Hazel, just… don’t interfere. Don’t show any favoritism.”

“…Yes, Master,” Hazel responded meekly.

She bowed her head in acknowledgment of Henry’s command, her demeanor conveying a mix of nervousness and resignation.

With hesitant steps, she moved away from the immediate vicinity of the would-be duel, taking her place as an unwilling observer.

“Alright, Let’s begin this match now, shall we?” Yoichi chuckled. “I suppose this will be a good way to stretch my muscles.”

Once Hazel had retreated to a safe distance, the impromptu duel commenced, the air thick with unspoken tension and simmering animosity.

---

Holding a long sword in one hand and a dagger in the other represents a time-honored and orthodox fighting style favored by many swordsmen, each blade designed for very specific purposes.

However, it differed significantly from the dual swordsmanship practiced by the butler, Vista.

Unlike true dual-wielding, where both swords move in concert while transitioning fluidly between offense and defense, Henry’s style was more rigid.

He had clearly defined, almost compartmentalized, roles for each weapon: the long sword for aggressive attacks and the dagger for parrying and defensive maneuvers.

In contrast, Yoichi casually held the dulled training dagger, the very weapon Henry had gifted him, in a reverse grip.

The training weapon was practical, nothing special about it.

“Seiyaaah—!!”

Henry was the first to move.

He had launched himself forward with a guttural shout, bringing his saber down in a powerful overhead slash, aimed directly at Yoichi’s head.

The attack was undeniably swift and forceful, a testament to Henry’s physical strength and dedicated training.

However,

_…Too slow._

Yoichi thought.

For Yoichi, who had endured the relentless and unorthodox training regime of Celestin, the attack seemed telegraphed, lacking any subtlety or deceptive feints.

It was like watching a predictable play unfold in slow motion.

He had deliberately tried to “reset” Henry’s state, hoping that his earlier aggression was simply due to a lack of composure, leading to sloppy movements.

However, even with this “reset,” Henry’s swordsmanship remained disappointingly predictable.

As Henry closed the distance, Yoichi nonchalantly switched the dagger to his left hand, his movements fluid and almost dismissive.

Then, with impeccable timing, he evaded the descending sword, the blade whistling past his ear.

Simultaneously, he intercepted the attack with the flat of his dagger, deflecting the blow with minimal effort.

The two blades collided with a dull thud.

“Mmph!?”

Henry grunted.

He, completely taken aback by the unexpected parry, could only manage a stunned exclamation.

He had anticipated overwhelming Yoichi with his superior swordsmanship, but his attack had been effortlessly neutralized.

Seizing upon Henry’s moment of hesitation, Yoichi grasped the guard of Henry’s saber with his right hand.

“Here we go,” Yoichi said with a grin.

“Wh-!?” Henry exclaimed, his eyes widening in alarm.

With a sharp, decisive motion, Yoichi wrenched the saber from Henry’s grasp and tossed it aside, sending it clattering across the training ground.

“Uaaah—!”

Henry screamed, completely shocked.

Disarmed and desperate, he instinctively thrust his dagger – his remaining weapon – forward with his left hand, attempting a counter-attack.

Just because the dagger was primarily for defense didn’t mean it couldn’t be used offensively, especially in a situation as dire as this.

“Hmph.”

“Guah!”

Before the dagger could reach its target, Yoichi delivered another strike – this time a precise hand chop to Henry’s left wrist, severing the connection between weapon and hand.

The dagger clattered to the ground, leaving Henry completely unarmed and vulnerable.

“Alright, that’s the end of the line,” Yoichi said.

In the very next breath, Yoichi pressed the tip of the dagger against Henry’s neck, the dulled metal a chilling reminder of the potential consequences of a real battle.

“Can we all agree that I won?”

Yoichi turned at the direction of the referee, his voice calm and even.

“Eh… ah…”

But the referee just stuttered.

Hazel, when asked by Yoichi, was frozen with indecision, her eyes darting back and forth between the two combatants.

She was only able to let out a confused, almost inaudible sound, unsure of how to respond to the unexpected turn of events.

“I’m… not done yeeeet!!”

Henry cried out loud. With a desperate roar fueled by wounded pride, he lunged forward, swinging a wild punch at Yoichi.

He clearly wasn’t thinking as the situation had changed.

If this were a real battle with live steel, Henry would have already been dead, his throat slit by Yoichi’s dagger.

However, knowing that they were using blunted training weapons, Henry recklessly attacked, disregarding the potential consequences.

Even though the dagger was dulled, it was still a formidable weapon.

Under the current parameters, a carefully aimed thrust could still incapacitate Henry, perhaps by piercing his throat.

However, Yoichi had absolutely no intention of harming Alana’s younger sibling.

With a swift backward leap, he effortlessly dodged the clumsy punch.

“Oh dear, it seems the match is continuing?”

It had been established that victory would be determined by surrender, death, or Hazel’s judgment.

“Um…”

Yet the quiet Hazel is still yet to respond.

“I haven’t lost yet!!”

Henry made another scream.

This adamant declaration cut across Hazel’s hesitant response.

Given the way things had unfolded, Hazel would probably never go against the wishes of her master Henry.

Not because she wanted to.

But rather because she had to.

“Well, I can’t say I don’t appreciate the tenacity,” Yoichi said with a shrug.

He let the dagger drop from his hand, letting it fall to the ground with a clattering sound.

“Come at me then I suppose. I’ll entertain you until you’re satisfied, little brother-in-law.”

Yoichi had already gleaned a fair understanding of Henry’s abilities using [Appraisal+], but a few more exchanges solidified his assessment.

He placed Henry at around C-rank for an adventurer, a level comparable to Graff’s strength back when he was still based in Meilgrad.

This meant, quite plainly, that Henry was no real match for Yoichi, whose skills had been dramatically honed through Celestin’s rigorous training.

As an interesting aside, the hero Graff, the “Crimson Flash,” had demonstrated remarkable growth since his duel with Yoichi and the subsequent Demon Invasion.

He’d also acquired enhanced equipment from the master craftsman Sam Smith and was reportedly on track for a promotion to B-rank in the near future.

It seemed even his old rival was showing significant progress.

“Waaaaaaah! Don’t make fun of meeeee!!”

Henry roared, charging forward, fist raised high.

Yoichi watched, a touch of bemusement on his face, as his opponent barreled towards him.

“Take this—!”

Henry yelled again, throwing a wide, albeit powerful, right straight aimed directly at Yoichi’s face.

But just before impact, Yoichi casually raised his left hand, effortlessly brushing the punch aside.

The difference in their speed and power was stark.

—Smack!

In the next instant, a sharp slap resounded as Yoichi’s open palm connected with Henry’s left cheek.

“Eh…?”

Henry uttered, a foolish sound escaping his lips.

He was bewildered, his mind struggling to process what had just occurred.

But the impact was confirmed as registered – the warmth blooming on his cheek and the crisp sound of the slap confirmed all that.

What about the pain? Well, it wasn’t nearly as significant as he anticipated.

Henry turned his face, which had been forcibly redirected by the slap, back towards Yoichi, only to find him still standing there, a picture of unperturbed calm.

“Aaaaaaaah—!!”

With a renewed roar, he forced himself back into action, launching a left hook toward Yoichi’s torso.

—Slap!

Yet again, Henry’s strike was easily batted away, as if swatting an irritating insect.

Another dry slap echoed, and a similar, though slightly sharper, sting flared across his right cheek this time.

From that moment onward, the fight devolved into a completely one-sided affair.

No matter what Henry attempted, Yoichi effortlessly deflected each blow.

Every feint, every strike, every desperate lunge was met with casual ease.

And invariably, the deflection was followed by another stinging slap to Henry’s increasingly reddened cheeks.

Even when he tried to grapple, a simple, light push to the chest was enough to completely halt his advance.

It felt like trying to move a massive boulder; he couldn’t close the distance even by a single millimeter.

Frustration mounting and energy draining, another slap landed, a constant, humiliating reminder of his helplessness.

“Still going?”

Yoichi asked, his voice devoid of any real challenge.

Henry’s cheeks, now bearing the brunt of over ten slaps on each side, were visibly inflamed and swollen.

The limited pain he felt was likely due to the surge of adrenaline coursing through his veins, a byproduct of his desperate combat.

However, the cumulative physical, and together with it, emotional damage inflicted was undeniable.

“Shut uuup!!”

Henry shouted, his voice cracking with a mixture of anger and frustration.

Seeing Henry stubbornly refusing to yield, Yoichi sighed softly and delivered a noticeably more forceful open-handed slap.

“Ugh…!”

The increased impact sent Henry stumbling backward, and he collapsed onto the ground.

“Ugh… ugh… not yet…” he groaned, struggling to regain his footing.

“Please, enough…!”

Then, all of a sudden, Hazel threw herself over him, effectively pinning him to the ground.

“G-Get off…”

Henry gasped, attempting to shove her away.

“Let’s stop this now, Henry…!”

Yet Hazel pleaded, wrapping her arms around her master from the front, desperately trying to quell his futile struggle.

“Don’t interfere…”

“I can’t…!”

“I haven’t lost yet…!”

Even as Hazel held him tight, Henry continued to glare at Yoichi, attempting to rise.

“You can’t win… Henry…”

Hazel said at last, her voice tinged with sadness.

“Shut up… I will win… I’ll win against him, and then with my sister…”

Henry’s words revealed the core of his motivation, the deep-seated desire to prove himself, not just to Yoichi, but to his own family member.

“That’s why I’m telling you it’s impossible, Henry!! Because…!”

But to this, Hazel exclaimed, shifting slightly away from him to stare at him directly in his eyes.

Then, she subtly pointed towards Yoichi with the hand that was hugging his back, conveying a crucial truth.

“That person isn’t even fighting seriously at all…!!”

The words hung in the air, stark and undeniable.

Henry, hearing those devastating words, froze completely, his eyes widening in disbelief and a dawning understanding.

The futility of his struggle crashed down upon him.

“Let’s stop now, okay…? Please?”

Hazel’s voice was now soft and imploring, filled with genuine concern.

Henry’s brow furrowed in a mixture of anguish and shame, and tears began to well up in the corners of his eyes.

He gritted his teeth, his entire body trembling with the effort to control his emotions, and yet still tried to stand.

Hazel immediately tightened her hold, hugging him even more firmly to prevent him from further embarrassing himself.

In the world of medicine, particularly within the ever-evolving field of psychiatry, common understanding frequently underwent seismic shifts in short spans of time.

Phenomena that were once relegated to the realm of mere idiosyncrasies were often reclassified, assigned diagnostic labels, and subjected to established treatment protocols.

In a country like the Kingdom, where feudalism still lingered, it was nearly impossible to retract a decision made in the name of the king, no matter how much exculpatory evidence was presented later.

## **Chapter 10 – A Messenger from the Royal Castle**

The next morning, Alana was awakened by a gentle but insistent knock at her door.

It was the mansion’s venerable butler and caretaker, his presence signaling that something important had transpired.

A visitor, he informed her, had arrived from the royal castle, requesting an immediate audience.

Yoichi, along with the women, who had also been roused by the early morning activity, quickly got ready.

When they stepped out of their rooms, the old butler stood patiently beside a young maid, both bowing their heads respectfully.

Alana’s first concern was for those affected by the previous night’s events.

“How is Henry?” she inquired, her voice tinged with concern.

“The Young Master appears to be resting in his room, my lady,” the butler replied, his voice hushed. “When I inquired, Hazel informed me that he is in no condition to be woken. She herself,” the butler added, “was also quite exhausted and still sleeping soundly, which is why I have come to you.”

Alana turned a worried gaze to Yoichi.

Soon as he met her eyes, he offered a reassuring nod.

“It’s best if Henry rests for a while,” he said, his tone calm. “Hazel will likely recover after half a day’s rest, so I think it’s fine to leave things to her after that.”

Yoichi have already assessed the situation using [Appraisal+].

The backlash from dispelling the charm had left Henry mentally and physically drained; he wouldn’t likely wake up for some time.

Hazel, on the other hand, was merely fatigued from their ‘session’ that was slightly more intense than usual; with proper sleep and food, she would soon recover fully.

The butler then continued, his tone shifting slightly to a more formal report.

“Also, last night, several Royal Guards came to see the witnesses in question. It appears they conducted an interrogation.”

He elaborated on the specifics: Kenneth and Leonard, the knights from House Colborne being held as witnesses, were being detained in the gatekeeper’s lodge outside the mansion.

Permission had been given for them to be interrogated freely, but on the strict condition that the gatekeeper, Guile, be present, and that anyone, no matter their status, must follow his instructions.

“I understand. Thank you for the detailed report, Butler,” Alana said, absorbing the information. “Now, regarding this visitor, who exactly is it?”

“It is the male Royal Guard who was guarding the Master’s bedroom last night, along with one other person, my lady,” the butler responded. “They arrived covertly and informed us they would not disclose their name or identity to anyone but the Young Master or the Young Mistress themselves.”

“Hmm. Do you recognize the other person?” Alana pressed, a hint of suspicion in her voice.

The butler shook his head. “Their face is concealed, so I could not make out any distinguishing features.”

Led by the old butler, the group proceeded to the reception room.

As they entered, they saw a figure clad in a hooded robe already seated on the guest sofa, with the male guard from yesterday standing silently behind them.

The visitor was wrapped tightly in their robe as if to utterly conceal their identity, the hood pulled down low over their eyes, obscuring everything but a hint of shadow.

Their appearance screamed ‘suspicious person,’ yet curiously, they didn’t exude any particular sense of menace.

Instead, they seemed to be enjoying their tea with an almost natural, unhurried air.

_I see, the robe must be enchanted,_ thought Yoichi, his [Appraisal] skill tingling.

Sensing something was subtly off about the visitor’s seemingly mundane presence, he activated the skill, instantly confirming his suspicion: the robe was indeed imbued with a powerful perception-inhibiting magic.

“You are Alana Salis, I presume?”

The voice that emerged from beneath the hood seemed equally altered, impossibly neutral, making it impossible to determine whether it was male or female, young or old.

Alana suppressed a mischievous thought—a line from a period drama about requesting another’s name first.

While she was surprisingly fond of the sentiment, she had no intention of actually throwing that specific line at her guest from the royal castle, at least not yet.

Instead, she chose to forgo the usual courtesies and identify herself by her professional standing.

“Indeed. I am Alana Salis, a B-rank adventurer.”

The male guard behind the robed figure confirmed, his voice clear. “We met yesterday. This is indeed Lady Alana Salis.”

A faint, almost musical chuckle emanated from beneath the hood.

“I too saw you from a distance when you visited the Royal Capital before. You have the same dignified and beautiful presence as ever.”

Alana met the unseen gaze, her expression unyielding.

“Flattery will get you nowhere. Now then, what business do you have with my family?”

The air in the reception hall, already thick with unspoken tension, seemed to solidify around them.

A subtle shift in the robed figure’s posture was the only indication of their reaction.

“If possible,” the voice, neither distinctly male nor female, but possessing a certain resonant depth, replied, “I would like to request an audience with Lord Henry… though I suppose that is currently difficult?”

The question hung in the air, a polite acknowledgment of the known truth.

“My younger brother is unwell and unable to leave his bed,” Alana confirmed, her expression hardening fractionally. “If this concerns the Salis family, I am currently acting as the lord of this domain. Therefore, you may present your case to me.”

“That is correct,” Alana stated, her posture straightening imperceptibly, an additional layer of authority settling upon her shoulders.

“In that case, I believe there is a certain etiquette that should be observed, is there not?” The guest’s voice took on a sharper edge, carrying a subtle undercurrent of command. “Being looked down upon while you stand there like that is not a particularly pleasant feeling, you see.”

At these words, Alana’s brow furrowed, a theatrical exaggeration that nevertheless conveyed her displeasure.

It was a clear challenge to the visitor’s veiled authority, a refusal to be intimidated.

“Then state your name,” she countered, her voice dropping to a low, dangerous register. “I am not possessed of the courtesy to be paid to one whose identity I do not know.”

“And yet, I believe you were told I came directly from the Royal Castle,” the robed figure retorted, a hint of steel entering their tone. “Is that not enough?”

“No matter where you’ve come from, to my eyes, you look like nothing more than a suspicious person hiding their face,” Alana replied, her gaze unwavering, even as her eyes seemed to pierce through the heavy folds of the traveler’s cloak.

“A suspicious person, you say?”

After uttering those words, the robed figure began to chuckle.

It was a low, guttural sound that seemed to rumble from deep within their chest, devoid of malice, yet brimming with a complex mix of amusement and something akin to admiration.

“I see… So this is how I appear now, a suspicious person… Heh heh heh… Just what I’d expect from the Princess Knight.”

It was true; the concealment effect of the robe this guest was wearing was quite potent.

An ordinary person wouldn’t even sense anything amiss; the figure seemed to absorb light and sound, becoming little more than a formless shadow.

But the guest seemed to be genuinely enjoying the fact that its concealing effect wasn’t working very well on Alana, as if her unique perception was a delightful confirmation of her reputation.

Meanwhile, the Royal Guard standing rigidly behind the guest wore a profoundly complicated expression.

From the very start, Alana’s attitude had been nothing but discourteous, bordering on outright defiant, toward a visitor from the Royal Castle – a visitor who, to the guard’s trained eye, carried an aura of immense power and authority.

However, should he react carelessly, he would risk giving Alana a crucial clue as to the true identity of his charge.

And so, he had no choice but to stand there, a silent sentinel of suppressed anxiety and an indescribable blend of frustration and grudging respect for Alana’s audacious spirit.

“I have no objection to giving my name,” the guest finally said, the chuckle fading into a more businesslike tone. “But, I must ask that anyone other than Lady Alana excuse themselves from the room.”

Their gaze swept over the butler and maid standing dutifully nearby.

At the guest’s words, the elderly butler bowed deeply, a silent command to the young maid, who curtsied gracefully.

Together, they turned and quietly left the room, their footsteps muffled as the heavy oak door swung shut behind them.

Confirming their departure with a sharp glance, Alana spoke, her voice still firm.

“My apologies, but I must ask for permission for my companions to remain.”

She gestured subtly towards Yoichi and the others, who stood patiently, observing the exchange with keen interest.

“Oh?” The guest’s head tilted slightly, a movement barely discernible beneath the heavy hood. “Then are these the renowned TOKOROTEN of whom the rumors speak?”

A flicker of curiosity, sharper than before, seemed to emanate from the shadowed face.

“Yes, they are my reliable companions,” Alana affirmed, her tone leaving no room for argument. “You may ask them to leave, but I will only end up explaining the situation to them myself afterward. Be warned, I have no intention of keeping silent, not even for a royal edict.”

Her eyes held a challenge, a testament to her fierce loyalty and independent spirit.

“Hmm…” The guest considered her words for a moment, a palpable silence filling the room before they spoke again. “In that case, allow me to verify their guild cards.”

The guard meticulously examined each one before offering a succinct report.

“There is no mistake,” the Royal Guard reported, his voice flat and professional. “All guild cards are authentic and registered to the adventurers known as TOKOROTEN.”

With a fluid, deliberate motion, they reached up and removed the voluminous, concealing robe.
