Their purplish-red eyes, striking against the pale complexion, were half-hidden by heavy eyelids, yet their gaze, when it met Alana’s, was astonishingly sharp and intelligent.

Fine wrinkles, like delicate etchings of experience, were visible at the corners of their eyes, and their smile lines were also etched somewhat deeply, hinting at a life well-lived and perhaps, a dry wit.

They appeared to be a woman, seemingly around fifty years old, yet possessed of a vibrant, almost ageless energy.

Her attire, now fully revealed, was a tightly tailored, one-piece-style coat that reached to around her knees.

It boasted a chic, restrained color scheme of deep forest green and charcoal, cut with a distinctly masculine silhouette that emphasized broad shoulders and a narrow waist.

Yet, the refined features of her face, and the subtle curve of a formidable bust pushing out the fabric from within, unequivocally confirmed that this powerful individual was, indeed, a woman.

And then, Alana’s gaze fell upon the crest embroidered with meticulous detail upon the left breast of the coat.

An intricate design of a soaring falcon clutching a golden lyre, it was a symbol she knew well from ancient texts and royal histories.

Her eyes widened, a gasp catching in her throat as recognition, astonishment, and a touch of awe washed over her face.

“Could it be… Duchess Tobias?”

The name escaped Alana’s lips, a hushed reverence in her tone.

Immediately, she lowered her head in a deep bow, a gesture Yoichi and the others swiftly mirrored, their expressions a mixture of surprise and deference.

A husky, yet remarkably pleasant voice drifted from the guest, who had now fully removed her travel cloak, revealing the elegant attire beneath.

“Oh my, to be known by the famous Princess Knight is an honor indeed. And this,” she added, a hint of amusement in her tone, “after I heard you had forgotten the crest of the Colborne family.”

Her words indicated she had already grasped the full scope of yesterday’s tumultuous events.

Alana straightened slightly, her voice carefully modulated.

“My apologies, Your Excellency, the Prime Minister. Our house, though a Margravate, is but a shadow compared to the prestige and influence you command.”

The visitor was indeed none other than Duchess Rosanna Tobias, the current Prime Minister herself.

“And so, for the Prime Minister herself to grace our humble home, what might be the meaning of this unexpected visit?” Alana inquired, her tone respectful yet direct.

“Before that, please, make yourselves comfortable.”

At Rosanna’s urging, Alana and Yoichi moved to sit on the opposing sofa, a clear sign that this was to be more than just a fleeting courtesy call.

Karin, Misato, and Xihan, demonstrating proper decorum, opted to remain standing a respectful distance behind them.

Rosanna began, her tone shifting to one of solemn gravity.

“First, regarding this recent matter: for casting undue suspicion upon the Margrave, who has rendered such great service to the Kingdom, I apologize. This visit, as you know, is unofficial, as is this apology, but I felt it imperative to offer it in person, here and now.”

With these words, the Prime Minister of the Kingdom, Duchess Rosanna Tobias, inclined her head in a deep, formal bow.

Though her arrival had been discreet, unannounced and unrecorded, the gesture itself carried immense weight – an unofficial acknowledgment from the highest authority.

Alana’s voice was tight with anticipation. “Does that mean my father’s name has been cleared?”

Rosanna met her gaze directly. “Yes, Lady Alana. Completely.”

A wave of visible relief washed over Alana’s features, though she maintained her composure.

“I understand, Your Excellency. I accept your apology, and I thank you for your swift action.”

Rosanna offered a small, knowing smile, the tension visibly easing from her shoulders. “Thank you.”

“So,” Alana pressed gently, “could you please tell us the details of the situation? How was this resolved so quickly?”

Rosanna nodded, getting straight to the heart of the matter.

“To be frank, Lady Alana, this whole affair has been swiftly concluded. It has been determined to be a baseless rumor, meticulously spread by Patrick Colborne solely to hide his personal grudges and his own egregious misdeeds. Officially, of course,” she added with a delicate emphasis, “We’ll be ensuring that, as far as public record is concerned, that ‘nothing happened’ at all.”

She elaborated further on the specifics. Mainly, the ‘confinement’ order issued to Lord William will be retroactively changed to a ‘standby’ order.

The official reasoning provided will be that the comprehensive report on the monster stampede and the Demon attack requires significant time for proper processing.

Naturally, all records will reflect that the order was ‘standby’ from its very inception, making it seem as though Lord William was never truly held against his will.

“The swift testimony of those two individuals you apprehended, Knight Kenneth and Knight Leonard, lent immediate and undeniable credibility to the preliminary report you submitted,” Rosanna continued. “Based on their confessions, Patrick Colborne’s entire series of accusations was unequivocally judged to be a deliberate fabrication.”

Alana, still processing the rapid turn of events, voiced her lingering doubt. “Even so, Your Excellency, I confess I find it hard to believe you would grace our home in person, barely a day after this began… The speed is truly remarkable.”

This was then when Rosanna’s expression grew serious.

“There are, in fact, several reasons for my haste, but the first, and most significant, is that the Empire has made a move.”

Both Alana and Yoichi echoed, “The Empire?”

“Yes, the Empire” Rosanna affirmed. “I’m still uncertain how they acquired the information, but we received an urgent inquiry asking if it was true that Lord William was being held captive in the royal capital.”

She elaborated further on the Empire’s precarious position.

“Given that there’s no guarantee a Demon Attack won’t occur again in the north, many of the Empire’s most skilled adventurers are currently stationed heavily along their northern frontier. This means they would be severely compromised, unable to adequately deal with a large-scale monster swarm if they were to invade from the southern frontier, which borders your father’s domain.”

Rosanna’s voice hardened slightly. “In such a scenario, they declared—unofficially, of course, presented as purely for ‘self-defense’—that their military would have no choice but to take over the defense of their southern frontier directly. This, naturally, would necessitate a significant military buildup along our shared border, and they insisted that the Kingdom ought to simply accept it.”

A low “Hmph” then escaped Rosanna. “As if they’d build up their military on the border and leave it at just ‘self-defense.’ A troublesome piece of information has fallen into the hands of a very troublesome group. I suspect a spy who had infiltrated the capital overheard Patrick spreading it around, perhaps boasting of his temporary victory.”

Unbeknownst to the Prime Minister, however, her speculation about the source was wide off the mark.

Yoichi, standing quietly behind Alana, consciously avoided eye contact.

He recalled his earlier conversation with Alec, how he had explained the dire situation regarding William’s “confinement” and Alec’s determined promise, “We’ll do what we can!”

It seemed Alec, in coordination with Celestin and Gisela, the Adventurers’ Guild Master in the northern frontier, had handled things with far more—and far swifter—skill than anyone could have anticipated.

Rosanna leaned forward slightly. “Therefore, as the Kingdom, we are compelled to declare definitively that Lord William’s absence from the frontier is merely temporary, a brief administrative interlude, and that he will be returning to his post shortly. In other words, we must forcefully assert that there is absolutely nothing amiss on the southern frontier, to dissuade any imperial adventurism.”

“I see,” Alana murmured, a new understanding dawning. “So that’s why this is all happening with such unprecedented speed…”

Alana had indeed predicted that once Patrick Colborne’s violent, baseless plot was thoroughly acknowledged, her father’s unjust confinement would soon be lifted.

But even she was taken aback by the sheer alacrity with which events were now unfolding.

“By the way, Your Excellency,” Alana interjected, “you mentioned earlier that there were ‘several reasons’ for your immediate intervention. Is there something else you wished to discuss?”

“Mm, yes, and on that matter, I must apologize to you once more, Princess Knight,” Rosanna admitted, her expression darkening slightly.

“Apologize?” Alana repeated, a hint of concern in her voice.

“Yes, that’s right. Regarding the crucial testimony about Patrick’s violent plot, we were only able to obtain it from the two knights, Kenneth and Leonard, whom you had so effectively restrained.”

Alana’s brow furrowed. “…Then what about the adventurers, Genber and his group? The ones who were supposed to have been apprehended alongside the knights? Were they not to corroborate the story?”

A grim shadow crossed Rosanna’s face.

“By the time our forces stormed the mansion, Lady Alana, they had all been killed. Brutally. To silence them, no doubt.”

She then elaborated on the likely sequence of events.

“It seems Patrick grew suspicious when Kenneth and Leonard didn’t return. When he checked the mansion where he had Genber and the others hiding, he must have discovered the captured ruffians—and then, in a fit of panicked rage, disposed of them all to tie up loose ends.”

Yoichi, listening intently, inwardly confirmed her speculation; his [Appraisal+] results from the scene had indicated much the same grisly truth.

“And so, having unmistakably sensed the danger closing in, Patrick fled the capital sometime last night.”

Alana’s voice betrayed her concern. “So he escaped… But in that case, Your Excellency, don’t you have too few witnesses to truly solidify your case? Even without Patrick, I would think that if the nobles who had sided with him were to resist, things wouldn’t proceed so smoothly.”

Rosanna’s expression became even more troubled, a hint of genuine bewilderment in her eyes. “That… is the strange thing, Lady Salis…”

Alana leaned forward, her curiosity piqued. “What do you mean?”

A deep sigh escaped the Prime Minister’s lips as her brow furrowed in evident frustration.

“The ones who were openly aligned with Patrick… every last one of them came forward this morning, without exception, to formally apologize for their purported involvement.”

“To apologize?” Alana repeated, her disbelief plain.

“Well, ‘apology’ might not be the most accurate word,” Rosanna conceded, a wry smile touching her lips. “More like an ‘excuse.’ A unified, almost rehearsed excuse. They all, without fail, offered the exact same explanation.”

Rosanna lowered her voice, her gaze sweeping over Alana and Yoichi, a troubled glint in her eyes.

“They all recited the exact same, preposterous claim.” She paused, letting the implication hang in the air for a moment before delivering the bombshell.

“‘We were being manipulated by Patrick and Amanda.’”

---

Amanda’s enthralling charm, while potent, suffers a significant degradation once someone is beyond the immediate reach of her magic.

While her influence normally blankets the entirety of the royal capital, ensuring widespread obedience, the moment she steps outside its boundaries, the effect of her spell drastically wanes.

It’s not akin to a complete rupture, as was proven with Henry, where the enchantment shattered entirely.

Instead, it merely recedes, lying dormant.

Should those who had fallen under her sway return within range or re-establish contact with her, the subtle, insidious hold of her magic would quickly resurface, reasserting itself with chilling efficiency.

“Patrick has probably returned to the Colborne Earldom,” Prime Minister Rosanna stated, her voice tight with exasperation.

“Probably?” Alana pressed, leaning forward. “If you suspect that, why can’t he be apprehended?”

“Naturally, we’ve put out wanted notices at every checkpoint, in every town, and in various other strategic locations,” the Prime Minister explained, running a tired hand through her light green hair. “However, despite these exhaustive efforts, he and his party aren’t falling into our net.”

“Then why do you believe he’s heading for his own territory?” Alana inquired, her brow furrowed.

“There have been multiple eyewitness reports of a carriage that precisely fits the description.”

Rosanna then further explained.

Travelers on the main roads and residents in the towns they traversed had clearly spotted a carriage that bore the insignia or distinct characteristics of the House of Colborne.

Of course, they couldn’t be entirely certain, as it was likely concealed with magic, but they were still able to confirm that a noble carriage, unmistakably heading from the royal capital toward the Colborne Earldom, was moving at a considerable speed.

Given the timing, there was little doubt that it was carrying Patrick and his cohorts.

“And yet,” Rosanna continued, her frustration growing palpable, “the guards at those very checkpoints and in those towns claim they don’t recall seeing any such carriage.”

This baffling inconsistency, which Rosanna didn’t know unfortunately, was Amanda’s doing.

Amanda had “charmed” them.

Her magic, capable of dominating both mind and will, typically required a deep, prolonged connection, often established through intimate relations or extended exposure to her aura.

However, for fleeting interactions, a brief, potent burst of her charm was enough to ensure compliance—or, crucially, to erase memories of their passage.

It was clear she had been subtly using her power to slip through vital checkpoints, rendering their guards oblivious to Patrick’s movements.

“We have sent pursuers and set up ambushes along the probable route,” Rosanna added, her voice laced with defeat, “but there’s no sign of them being caught. All we’re getting are these frustrating, unconfirmed eyewitness accounts.”

The very act of extending her charm so broadly, however, had come at a cost.

By extending her magical influence so broadly across the kingdom’s travel routes, Amanda was inadvertently stretching her power thin.

As a direct consequence, her once iron-clad hold over the nobles and officials remaining within the capital had weakened even further, allowing many to break free from her insidious control, if only temporarily.

“So, what will happen if Patrick does make it back to his territory?” Alana asked, her question cutting through the prime minister’s worn resignation.

Most noble territories within the kingdom were granted a significant degree of autonomy.

The fief’s citizens, its knights, and its standing army often pledged their primary loyalty to their lord rather than directly to the king, and this feudal bond was particularly strong within the domain’s capital.

Thus, even if a royal edict were swiftly issued demanding Patrick’s surrender after he had sought refuge in his own lands, there was a significant chance they would outright refuse to comply.

On top of that, Amanda, the source of this kingdom-wide turmoil, was by his side.

With her potent charm, she could likely control not only the local order of knights but also the domain capital’s army and residents, bending them to Patrick’s will to a disturbing extent.

“It will likely come to a subjugation…” Rosanna said, scowling deeply at the grim prospect.

The Colborne Earldom, situated northeast of the royal capital, might not boast an exceptionally vast territory, but it was strategically vital, serving as one of the kingdom’s key hubs for trade with the powerful Empire.

If Patrick, faced with an overwhelming royal subjugation force, were to desperately appeal to the Empire for military assistance, it would instantly escalate into an extraordinarily troublesome international matter, potentially sparking a wider conflict.

“If that grim scenario unfolds,” Rosanna concluded, her jaw tight, “we will have no choice but to officially strike him down as a traitor to the crown.”

Assisting a declared traitor was a clear and undeniable act of hostility against the kingdom.

If the royal court were to send a subjugation force for a lesser crime, it was conceivable that the Empire, upon being petitioned for help, might step in to mediate a reconciliation – demanding a hefty fee for their intervention, no doubt.

However, they would almost certainly not risk committing such a blatant act of hostility as openly supporting a proven traitor.

“But in that case, we would also be compelled to punish all those who sided with Patrick,” Rosanna restarted the conversation, her gaze distant, calculating the devastating ripple effects.

If they were to charge Patrick with treason, they would have to fabricate a litany of severe accusations, starting with how he cast baseless suspicion on William, incited the frontier against the kingdom, and conspired to sap the very strength of the nation.

In such a scenario, the numerous nobles, bureaucrats, and military officials who had publicly followed Patrick’s lead and called for William’s punishment would also have to be appropriately and severely penalized.

This would undoubtedly plunge the kingdom into unprecedented chaos, potentially shattering its delicate political balance.

“If only we could capture him on his way…” the Kingdom’s Prime Minister murmured, letting out a long, weary sigh.

She probably understood that such hope was slim to none.

“Honestly… manipulating people to this extent… just what is this man’s goal? And who is this Amanda in the first place?” Rosanna prated further, her frustration evident.

Of course, Rosanna had also been investigating Amanda.

And not just recently, but from the very beginning, when Patrick first started to denounce William.

Her name had come up soon after they started investigating Patrick, but in the end, her identity remained an infuriating mystery.

Seeing the prime minister sigh so powerlessly, Alana looked at Yoichi and gave a firm, almost imperceptible nod. Taking her cue, Yoichi cleared his throat.

“Um, Your Excellency, the Prime Minister.”

Yoichi stepped forward, his voice calm and clear.

Rosanna’s tired eyes, usually sharp and calculating, darted towards him. “Hm? You are… Lord Yoichi, if I recall?”

Her tone was still edged with the day’s frustrations, a fact she seemed to quickly regret but didn’t bother to apologize for.

Yoichi, perfectly understanding her irritation, offered a small, reassuring smile.

“Yes, that’s right. And I believe there is something crucial I can inform you of.”

“Oh? Does Lord Yoichi have some brilliant idea to offer?” Rosanna winced, realizing her tone had been sharper than intended, a mere reflection of her deep irritation.

Yet, she didn’t go out of her way to apologize.

Yoichi, understanding her agitated state, didn’t seem to mind in the slightest.

“I don’t claim to possess a brilliant plan, Your Excellency,” Yoichi replied smoothly, “but there is one crucial piece of information I can certainly provide—”

“Hmm… I hear Lord Celestin’s right-hand man is remarkably well-versed in matters of intelligence.” Rosanna’s eyes narrowed, a flicker of professional curiosity replacing her frustration.

“I’m honored to hear you say that,” Yoichi acknowledged with a slight bow of his head.

“So, what will you tell me? Are you going to claim you know Amanda’s true identity?” Rosanna challenged, a skeptical twist to her lips.

“As expected of the Prime Minister,” Yoichi responded, a ghost of a smile touching his lips. “You’re very perceptive.”

“Is that true!?”

Rosanna shot up from her seat, her eyes wide with disbelief and an almost frantic hope, leaning so far forward she nearly toppled the low table between them.

A quick cough, however, brought her back to composure, a flush of embarrassment coloring her cheeks as she settled back down.

“Ahem… And?” she prompted, her voice now barely a whisper, though the sharp gaze from her reddish-purple eyes still pierced Yoichi.

He could feel the unspoken warning: Say anything foolish, and I won’t show you any mercy.

Without seeming to mind the Prime Minister’s formidable attitude in the slightest, Yoichi stared back at Rosanna with a perfectly nonchalant expression.

For just a fleeting moment, Rosanna felt herself being utterly overwhelmed by his composed, unwavering demeanor, a man who seemed to have no fear.

Then, while still gazing intently into the prime minister’s demanding eyes, Yoichi slowly opened his mouth, delivering the truth in a calm, measured tone.

“She’s a Demon.”

---

The Kingdom’s Prime Minister remained frozen for a while, her eyes and mouth wide open, the name “Demon” seeming to echo in the sudden silence of the room.

The male Royal Guard standing behind her was similarly stunned, his face pale.

“A Demon… you say…?” Rosanna finally whispered, the words barely audible.

The light returned to her somewhat vacant eyes, now fixed on Yoichi with a gaze weaker than before.

“Did you truly say… a Demon? Amanda is a Demon…?”

“Yes.” Yoichi affirmed, his voice steady.

“There was a Demon… in the royal capital? How could this be…? This is… preposterous!” Rosanna muttered, shaking her head, trying to process the impossible information.

Her initial disbelief quickly gave way to a sharp, strategic question. “Wait! Lord Yoichi, how did you find that out?”

“It’s a secret.”

“What?! A-Are you messing with me?!” Rosanna sputtered, caught off guard by his bluntness.

“No, I’m not. It’s an adventurer’s secret,” Yoichi replied, unperturbed.

“An adventurer’s… I see…”

Rosanna’s expression softened as the implications registered.

Adventurers often concealed their own abilities.

This could serve to increase their own value, but in most cases, it was for self-preservation.

Alternatively, it could be a confidential matter due to an agreement with the Guild.

In any case, when an adventurer said something was a secret, you couldn’t make them talk, not even with a royal decree.

Forcing them to speak was synonymous with making an enemy of the Adventurers’ Guild.

“Assuming Amanda is a Demon, what about the nobles being manipulated?” Rosanna pressed, her mind already shifting to the practicalities.

“That would be her ability. It seems Amanda can freely manipulate people by strongly charming them.”

“Freely… manipulating people… huh.” Rosanna chewed on the words, a grim line forming on her lips.

“However, it’s limited to male targets.”

“Limited to… men?” Rosanna repeated, and somehow, those words clicked perfectly into place.

She herself had been wondering: if Patrick could truly manipulate people, why had she not been targeted?

The puzzle pieces began to fall into a disturbing pattern.

“It’s a good thing the Prime Minister is a woman. After all, if she had made a move to Your Excellency, the Margrave likely wouldn’t have come out of this unscathed, and neither would her manipulation have cut off short,” Yoichi stated, a hint of dry amusement in his tone.

What Yoichi said was true.

If the goal was to have William executed and obtain the position of Margrave, manipulating Rosanna would have been the quickest way.

No, if Amanda had been so inclined, she might have been able to take over the entire kingdom.

Come to think of it, the king himself had seemed to be lacking his usual spirit lately…

“Don’t tell me, His Majesty was being manipulated, too?” Rosanna gasped, her eyes widening in horror.

“I’d imagine he was influenced to some extent. But it seems you have to have sex with someone to charm them completely.”

“Sex…? I see…”

This was another thing that rang a chilling bell.

Most of the nobles who had sided with Patrick were a less-than-reputable bunch, notorious for their carousing.

However, among them were several competent bureaucrats and key military figures who had been close to William, all of whom had suddenly and inexplicably begun currying favor with Patrick.

Until she learned of the charming ability, their motives had been unclear, but on reflection, it seemed that many in Patrick’s faction were indeed a lecherous sort.

“But… really, a Demon in the Royal Capital…? If that’s true… no, wait.” A fierce, almost predatory light ignited in Rosanna’s eyes, which had been bewildered until now.

Her mind, sharp and politically astute, was rapidly sifting through the implications.

The impossible revelation was transforming into an unprecedented opportunity.

“Even if it isn’t true… hmm… I see, a Demon… yes… excellent… Excellent! Kuhuhu… Hahahahaha…!”

With her eyes wide and gleaming, a twisted, almost gleeful smile forming on her lips, Rosanna’s gaze fixed upon Yoichi, startling him for just a moment.

“Lord Yoichi,” she purred, her voice dripping with a newfound admiration mixed with something darker, “you are quite the schemer, indeed.”

“Hah,” Yoichi grunted, a hint of unease crossing his face.

“That’s right! Whether Amanda is a Demon or not, even if it isn’t true, it’s not a problem at all! In fact, it’s the _perfect_ solution!” she exclaimed, her voice rising with excitement.

“Well, it is true, though,” he said, almost as an afterthought.

“Kuhuhuhu… Excel… lent…” Ignoring Yoichi’s quiet correction, Rosanna once again retreated into her own world, muttering, “With this, the Empire won’t be able to interfere… and I’ll have something to hold over those incompetent nobles and the arrogant military…!”

She was clearly envisioning a scenario where everything could be blamed on this convenient revelation. “Of course, it’s not something we can publicly announce—that a Demon had infiltrated the Royal Capital and, to make matters worse, had been manipulating a portion of the nobility and key military figures.”

Her thoughts now organized, a slightly calmer Rosanna began to explain her reasoning to Yoichi and the others.

However, her excitement hadn’t fully subsided; her eyes were still a little bloodshot and her breathing ragged.

“But we _can_ report this confidentially to the Empire. This time, it just so happened that a Demon had been allowed to infiltrate our Royal Capital, but it wouldn’t have been strange if the target had been the Imperial Capital instead. After all, much about the existence of Demons remains unknown.”

She continued, her voice gaining a strategic edge. “What if the abilities of a Demon—a single one of which is said to rival an entire army—were specialized for infiltration and espionage? Over there, the Prime Minister and most other key positions are held by men. Honestly, they could have dominated the Empire far more easily. What a foolish Demon.”

Since the Empire could very well think, “it could be us next,” they would be unlikely to publicly condemn the Kingdom for allowing a Demon to infiltrate the Royal Capital.

And if the Kingdom properly shared its intelligence on the Demon, then even if Patrick were to ask the Empire for aid, they would not grant it.

After all, the Demon Lord’s army, to which the Demon belong, is the enemy of all humanity.

To support Patrick, who sides with a Demon, would be a betrayal of humankind.

That would mean making an enemy of the Guild, and the hearts of their own subjects would surely turn away from them as well.

“In other words,” Rosanna concluded, a predatory gleam in her eye, “we can just trump up some suitable charge for Patrick and get rid of him. And those who sided with him, even if they were being manipulated, can’t be let off scot-free.”

They, too, could be charged with some appropriate crime and receive a suitable punishment.

All while hinting at the crime of treason, of course.

“If that happens, even the incompetent ones will likely become a bit more diligent. The stubborn bureaucrats and the arrogant military will probably become a little more obedient.”

This incident, which could have escalated into a disturbance great enough to shake the nation, was shaping up to have a very convenient resolution for the Prime Minister.

“It seems you’ve come up with a brilliant plan, Your Excellency,” Alana said in a calm tone, addressing the excitedly speaking Rosanna.

“Ah. Thanks to you all, it looks like many things will go well. This crisis has, unexpectedly, become an opportunity.”

“I am very glad to hear that. So, when might my father be released?” Alana pressed gently, her focus unwavering from her primary concern.

At Alana’s question, Rosanna looked blank for a moment, then immediately gave an apologetic smile.

“My apologies, I forgot to tell you in my excitement.”

The Prime Minister cut herself off there, cleared her throat, and composed her expression, shifting back to her official persona.

“The official notice will come later, but as of this moment, I hereby rescind the standby order for William, the Margrave of Salis. He is free to return to his duties immediately.”

Hearing Rosanna’s declaration, sighs and murmurs of relief escaped from Alana, Yoichi, and the other members.

“Thank you, Your Excellency, the Prime Minister. We are truly grateful,” Alana said, bowing her head slightly.

“The fault lies entirely with us; Lord William bears no blame whatsoever. This is truly not something you need to thank us for,” Rosanna replied, a genuine warmth in her smile.

At each other’s words, Alana and Rosanna looked at each other and shared a knowing, relieved smile.

“Ah, in that case, I’ll go inform the Margrave right away!” the Royal Guard said, his face breaking into a wide grin.

He had been standing silently throughout, clearly relieved by the outcome.

“Yes, please do. He will surely be pleased,” Rosanna nodded.

Having decided the Prime Minister no longer needed his protection, the Royal Guard left the room and ran off at a brisk pace, eager to deliver the good news.

“Ah! This is bad! This is bad, this is _really_, really bad…!”

Yoichi cried out, shooting to his feet with an urgency that stunned the Prime Minister.

“What is it, Lord Yoichi?” Alana asked, her brow furrowing with concern as Yoichi looked around frantically, as if searching for something missing.

Without answering Alana’s question, Yoichi muttered to himself, his eyes wide with sudden realization, before dashing out of the room.

“Now is a bad time for that!!” he shouted, his voice echoing down the hallway.

The remaining women, though tilting their heads at his bizarre behavior, exchanged bewildered glances before also standing up and following after him at a light run, a sense of foreboding beginning to settle over them.

“KYAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAH!!!!”

And just as Alana, who was in the lead, was about to catch up to Yoichi, a woman’s bloodcurdling scream echoed throughout the mansion, chilling them to the bone.

+++

## **Chapter 11 – A Messenger from the Royal Castle 2 ※**

When Yoichi finally caught up to the male royal guard, who was the first to respond to the screaming voice, he found the man standing stock-still in the open doorway of the bedroom, frozen like a statue.

His eyes were wide, his jaw was slack, and he seemed completely oblivious to Yoichi’s arrival.

“Excuse me.”

Yoichi gently but firmly pushed the dazed man aside.

He widened the door’s opening and stepped into the scene, which he could only describe as absolute chaos.

The air inside was thick, warm, and musty. And it smelled of sweat, perfume, and something distinctly… intimate.

Footsteps hurried up the hallway behind him.

“Mister Yoichi, that scream just now… what in the…?”

The first to arrive was Alana.

Upon reaching him, she immediately asked for the situation, only for her voice to trail off as she and the other women entered the room from behind him.

Just like the guard, she and the other women all came to an abrupt halt, their eyes stretching wide at the bewildering tableau before them.

Just then, another voice purred in with amusement.

“Oh my, everyone’s here. How embarrassing, to be caught in such a state… ufufu…”

It was none other than Margravine Isabel, the first wife of William who was currently on “standby” for being accused of rebellion.

She was, at this very moment, completely naked.

Yet, maybe there was still some shame left in her, or maybe its because of the Prime Minister’s presence, that she still managed to slip a silk gown over her shoulders albeit in a casual manner as if grabbing a coat to stroll at a park.

Still, the body of the woman, who looked to be in her late forties, was undeniably captivating.

Her breasts had resisted the full pull of gravity, and her rear maintained a firm, round shape.

While her stomach had a soft roundness to it, it wasn’t unsightly.

Rather, it even added an aura of mature, confident sensuality.

Her skin, right now, is glistening here and there with sticky bodily fluids, and as she moved, a thick, cloudy-white trickle would snake down her inner thigh before being thankfully hidden by the gown.

Yoichi’s eyes darted around the rest of the room, taking in the full scope of the pandemonium.

Sprawled on a large sofa, a younger woman who looked to be in her mid-twenties was fast asleep, her own gown having fallen completely open.

A single, firm breast was exposed, a stark and youthful contrast to Lady Isabel’s mature figure, which, while impressive, was just beginning to show the first hints of time’s passage.

From a bathroom in the back of the suite, someone was humming a jaunty tune, blissfully unaware of—or perhaps indifferent to—the scream that had summoned them all.

And then there was the main event.

_On the bed._

“Guoooooh… it hurts, it hurts so much…!”

There was Margrave William, his face a mask of agony.

He was locked in an embrace with the very female royal guard who had been posted outside his door the previous night.

He was groaning and sweating, still penetrating her from behind. All while the other party was completely limp, her head lolling to the side as if she’d lost consciousness.

# **Epilogue**

Stepping out of a much-needed shower, William felt… well, ‘refreshed’ was one word for it.

The aftermath of his encounter with Patricia had left him both drained and invigorated.

After straightening his clothes and making himself look at least somewhat presentable, he pushed open the door to the reception room, a slightly sheepish look on his face.

“My apologies for the, uh… unsightly scene earlier,” he began, his booming voice a little more subdued than usual.

Incidentally, Patricia had completely fainted upon reaching her climax and was now sleeping it off peacefully.

Isabel, ever the reliable wife, was currently by her side looking after her.

“Not at all, Margrave,” the Prime Minister, Rosanna, replied from the same sofa she’d occupied before.

A teasing, knowing smile played on her lips. “I’m just glad to see you’re still so energetic. It speaks well of your stamina… _Fufufu_.”

Behind her, the Royal Guard who stood as her silent protector seemed to be breathing just a little heavier than protocol dictated, his professional composure strained by whatever sounds had made their way through the walls.

When Rosanna gestured, Alana was already seated on the plush sofa opposite the Prime Minister.

The briefing was over.

“It’s a brilliant plan, just as I’d expect from you. Truly, something I could never have conceived of myself. It’s magnificent. _However_… that’s only if you can successfully subjugate Patrick in the first place.”

The Colborne Earldom is a major transportation hub now, but in the kingdom’s early days, it was a lawless land, crawling with bandits.

It was a key strategic point, which also made it a land that was easily targeted, and it had been built accordingly to oppose that.

# **Afterword**

Author: Hochi

Hey everyone, thanks for always reading “Eh, Failure to Transition!? …Success?”!

It’s your author, Hochi.

With Volume 11, I was so excited to finally get to write more about characters who only made brief appearances early on in the story, like Count Colborne, William’s wives, and Henry. It was a ton of fun to flesh them out!

Now, the original plan was for the story to progress much further in this volume.

But with all the new backstory chapters and new characters popping up, I got a little carried away, and the big conclusion with Patrick has been postponed until the next volume. My bad!

Because of that, we had to completely change the cover and illustrations from our initial plan.

I ended up causing a whole lot of trouble for our amazing illustrator, Saraki, especially during the super-busy end-of-year season.

Thank you, as always, for your absolutely wonderful illustrations! You’re a lifesaver!

With all that said, please look forward to Volume 12, where the showdown with Patrick and the female Demon, Amanda, will finally be settled (at least, it should be)!

++++

Having officially, if reluctantly, accepted the subjugation order for Alana’s cousin, Patrick, their first move was to get a detailed map from Prime Minister Rosanna.

Now, Yoichi was meticulously marking up every defensive mechanism his [Appraisal+] skill had uncovered, turning a simple map into a blueprint of the nightmare ahead.

Xihan then spoke up, pointing one of her beautifully-painted nails at a dense cluster of red circles surrounding the city.

“First things first. We’ve gotta do somethin’ about these landmine-lookin’ things.”

Just as she said, countless interception-type magic circles, effectively magical landmines, were buried in the earth around the provincial capital.

Karin narrowed her eyes at the sheer number of them.

“These are normally deactivated, though, right? It’d be insane to keep them armed all the time.”

As if anticipating for this answer, Yoichi spoke readily, rubbing the bridge of his nose.

“Yeah, they’re supposed to be. But Patrick declared a state of emergency the second he got back to his capital. He sealed the whole city.”

“So that means every single one of those traps is active right now. What about the people…?”

The last one was Misato. her usual quiet demeanor was now laced with concern.

The emergency declaration, issued in the lord’s name, had instantly forbidden anyone from entering or leaving Fallon.

For those already on the road, there was no warning.

Word eventually spread, but not before a number of travelers and merchants, unaware of the danger, had stepped into the newly activated minefield.

The casualties were already mounting.

“I had heard rumors of this defense system. But I never imagined he would actually use it. To turn it against his own people…”

Prime Minister Rosanna, who had joined them for the initial briefing, said with a heavy sigh.

It was a system designed for a foreign invasion, a last-ditch effort that could completely sever the capital from the outside world.

Even if it was only temporary, activating it was a massive breach of trust.

The fear it generated would likely scare away traders and travelers for years to come, a devastating blow for a city like Fallon that thrived on commerce.

It was clear Patrick was no longer thinking about consequences; he was a cornered animal.

“Normally, ya only hole up for a siege when ya know ya got reinforcements comin’. Who’s he expectin’ to bail him out?”

Xihan mused, scratching her chin.

Yoichi tapped the map at a certain location—the Empire.

After seeing how sloppy Patrick’s methods were, Yoichi had used [Appraisal+] to peek into his recent thoughts.

“Get this. Apparently, his brilliant plan was to go crying to the Empire for help. He’s been in back-channel talks with them for a while, building just enough of a relationship to get some Imperial nobles to help him in a pinch.”

Alana clenched her fist, her knuckles white.

“Honestly… To think my own main family would betray the kingdom for the Empire… how deplorable.”

“Well, that plan is already dead in the water. Thanks to some quick thinking on Her Excellency’s part.”

Yoichi glanced toward the female Prime Minister.

That hope of Imperial aid was utterly crushed the moment this woman learned Amanda’s true identity.

Just before Patrick even reached the safety of his capital, Rosanna had sent an urgent, discreet message to her contacts within the Empire.

She leaked the existence of the “Demon Person,” Amanda, and warned them in no uncertain terms not to get involved unless they wanted that chaos on their own doorstep.

“And as a result, Patrick was unceremoniously abandoned by his new friends.”

“Wait. So, let me get this straight, Yoichi. Does this pathetic Count even know that his precious Amanda is a Demon Person?”

Karin, looking baffled, cut in.

Yoichi gave a small, weary shake of his head as an answer.

“Nope. Not only does he not know, he doesn’t even suspect it. The thought literally can’t enter his head.”

He then proceeded to explain on how Patrick was so thoroughly ensnared by Amanda’s charm magic that he perceived any accusation against her as a personal attack.

In his mind, she was a flawless victim, and the idea that her presence could be a detriment to him was completely impossible.

Yoichi continued.

“He did get one final offer from the Empire, though. Something along the lines of, ‘we’re not unwilling to help you, but only if you hand over the woman, Amanda’. He took it as a personal insult.”

Patrick was now utterly convinced that Prime Minister Rosanna calling Amanda a “Demon Person” was just a vile political scheme to slander him.

His rage towards the kingdom was only growing, cementing his resolve to fight back.

“Okay, so he’s got no backup and he’s not thinkin’ straight. But how’s the Count plannin’ to resolve this whole mess, Yangyi? He can’t stay locked up forever.”

“He seems to think that if he repels a few of the kingdom’s subjugation teams, our side will get nervous and soften its stance. Then, he believes he can negotiate some kind of compromise and get away with it all.”

Yoichi explained to Xihan, who had summarized the situation.

“What a dangerously naive way of thinking…”

Misato also winced at the end.

Even Karin’s expression was turning serious.

“But what if he gets desperate, Alana? It’d be a lot trickier if he decides to take the citizens hostage, right?”

“Hmm… That’s true…. The people of Fallon were her people, too, in a way. If he uses them as a shield…”

Alana groaned, her own expression darkening at the thought.

That was the most terrifying part.

The defensive mechanisms in Fallon weren’t limited to just magical landmines.

While the towering walls and deep outer moats were standard, Yoichi’s [Appraisal+] had uncovered something far more sinister, a relic of a more brutal age.

“He has more than just the citizens as a hostage,” Yoichi said grimly, drawing their attention back to the map.

He pointed to five new marks he’d made: one in the exact center of the city, and four at the cardinal points. “He has the entire city.”

A heavy silence fell over the room.

“What do you mean?” Alana asked, her voice breaking the silence first.

Yoichi began to explain, his tone flat.

“These are large-scale magical facilities, built into the city’s foundation. They’re designed to destroy the bedrock beneath the capital. A self-destruct device—”

“—So you mean if that thing is activated, the whole town will literally sink into the underground water veins. Gone, in a single night?”

Karin finished his sentence, understanding dawning in her eyes.

“Which means we really, really need to avoid a situation where he decides to take the town down with him!?”

She stared at the map, at the thousands of lives represented by that piece of parchment.

The loss of a trading hub like Fallon would be a massive blow to the kingdom, but the real tragedy would be the people.

They weren’t just subjects of Count Colborne; they were citizens of the Kingdom of Sansrival.

“I see. If he demands some kind of settlement with the lives of everyone in the capital as his bargaining chip, it would be almost impossible for the kingdom to refuse him outright, wouldn’t it?”

Alana’s voice was tight with anger and fear.

Yoichi saw the tension gripping her and placed a reassuring hand on her shoulder.

“Hey. It’s a nasty setup, but if we get serious, we can handle it. That’s why your father trusted us with this whole mess, right? Not the royal knights, but us.”

He said softly, making her look at him.

A flicker of her usual resolve returned to Alana’s eyes.

“Mm, you’re right,” she said, managing a small, determined smile.

Yoichi then clapped his hands together, drawing everyone’s focus.

With a confident tone, he announced.

“Alright then. We know the layout, we know the traps, and we know the worst-case scenario. Let’s start figuring out how to take this whole thing apart, piece by piece.”

And so, with a renewed sense of purpose, the TOKOROTEN strategy meeting continued long into the night.

+++

## **Chapter 1 – In-charge of TOKOROTEN’s Rear**

The day after their big strategy meeting, Yoichi and Karin made their way back to Meilgrad.

Their first stop was Samantha’s workshop, a place that always smelled of strange magical reagents, hot metal, and ozone.

Inside, the scene was one of intense, almost comical, concentration.

Yoichi was hunched over a workbench, looking completely dazed as he painstakingly sketched geometric patterns onto a piece of parchment.

His tongue was sticking out of the corner of his mouth, a clear sign he was struggling.

Next to him, Samantha leaned in close, her sharp eyes peering at his wobbly lines.

“Hey, Yoichi,” she said, tapping a finger on a section of his drawing. “This curve here… isn’t it supposed to be more of a sharp angle, connecting to _this_ rune?”

Yoichi blinked, his focus breaking.

“Hmm? Oh…”

He squinted at the parchment, then at the air in front of him, as if recalling a mental image.

“You’re right. It is. Dang it.”

He scrubbed at the line with an eraser, smudging the ink.

“Yeah, the mana flow wouldn’t connect otherwise. It would just fizzle out.”

Samantha added, already taking a spare piece of paper to sketch the correct version from memory.

“Hmm, I feel like I’m missing something fundamental here…”

Around the middle, Yoichi groaned again, dropping his head into his hands.

He was trying his best to convey the intricate shapes of the magical landmines they’d found set up around Fallon, but it was like trying to describe a symphony to someone using only hand gestures.

His brain had a perfect picture thanks to his [Appraisal+] skill, but his hands just weren’t cooperating.

Ideally, Samantha would just go to Fallon and see the traps for herself.

But that presented a whole new set of problems.

The trip itself would take precious time, and more importantly, they couldn’t just keep changing the home point for his [Return+] skill.

It was a logistical nightmare that made this tedious drawing session their best, and most frustrating, option.

“If it’s within an hour, you can cancel the return and just pop back, right? Why not just go once so she can see them in person?”

Karin, who had been observing from the side with a mix of pity and amusement, finally spoke up.

Yoichi sighed, lifting his head.

“I thought about that, but if we do that, we have to commit to coming back here within the hour. Every single time. Considering all the work we still have to do on the other side, it’s just too tight.”

By “the other side,” he meant his original world, Earth, a place that was becoming just as demanding as this one.

“I also really need to consult with Charlotte about a few things, and you know how time back there can pass in the blink of an eye when you’re busy, not to mention going back and forth before a one-hour cool down is just…”

After weighing all the pros and cons, Yoichi had come to the frustrating conclusion that this was the most efficient way: he would use [Appraisal+] to memorize the magic circles, then try to replicate them in his clumsy drawings for Samantha to analyze and perfect.

“But seriously… will she ever get it with my crappy drawings?”

“Stop complaining and keep drawing, Yoichi. We don’t have all day.”

Karin spoke to Yoichi, crossing her arms at his smudged, crooked mess of a diagram.

“Here, Karin, look at this. I’m pretty much finished with the first one.”

As they were in the middle of it, Samantha held up her own sheet of paper, which made Karin widen her eyes in surprise.

“Seriously? You got all that from his chicken scratch?” She spoke as she leaned in.

“Yeah, somewhat. As long as you can grasp the core principles, the rest of the pattern falls into place. It’s like a puzzle.”

Samantha said with a confident smile.

On her paper was a perfectly rendered, complex magic circle, glowing with a faint trace of mana.

She had taken Yoichi’s shaky, 70% complete sketch and, with a spark of genius, accurately guessed the remaining components to finish it.

Yoichi’s face lit up with a small, defiant victory.

“See, Karin! Look! If she can figure _that_ much out from my drawing, it means I’m not completely useless, right?”

“Not _completely_ useless, no,” Karin conceded, tapping her chin thoughtfully.

“But no matter how you look at it, your art skills are still tragic.”

“She’s right, you know,” Samantha too chimed in, not unkindly.

“Like Yoichi, if you could just draw a straight line, I think Karin and I would have understood this a lot faster.”

“Ugh… you two are ganging up on me.”

Yoichi grumbled, slumping in his chair like a scolded child.

He was sulking, but he couldn’t deny the truth in their words.

Still, even with his artistic shortcomings, they had managed to fully decipher one of the enemy’s traps in just half a day.

It was proof that his brute-force method of memorizing and drawing wasn’t a complete mistake.

“Alright, don’t look so satisfied with yourself yet. We’ve only finished _one_ so far, right? How many different kinds did you say there were?”

Karin said, breaking his brief moment of pride.

Yoichi’s face fell.

“Damn it… there are still dozens of types.”

The sheer scale of the task ahead settled over them like a heavy blanket.

Drawing dozens of these things would take them weeks.

As the mood in the workshop soured, Samantha suddenly held up a hand.

“Wait a minute. I don’t think we have to analyze every single one of them from scratch.”

She said, her brow furrowed in thought.

“Really?”

Yoichi perked up.

Samantha nodded, then her expression turned sharp and focused.

“Yeah. But to be sure, I’d still like to see the components of as many different types as possible. Just the basics.”

“I see…”

Grabbing his quill again, a renewed sense of hope can be seen in Yoichi’s eyes.

He quickly sketched out the core patterns of several more magic circles.

This time, having already grasped the fundamental structure from the first one, Samantha’s analysis was lightning-fast.

She wasn’t just looking at the whole picture anymore; she was deconstructing it.

“Okay, stop.”

She said suddenly, taking the quill from him.

She circled a small, specific sequence of runes on the completed diagram.

“This part right here. This is the activation trigger and the mana source connection. It’s the heart of the trap.”

Then she looked up at Yoichi.

“How many of the other magic circles you saw have this _exact_ same component?”

“Hold on a minute…”

Yoichi closed his eyes, activating [Appraisal+] and focusing his mind on the minefield in Fallon.

Instead of looking at whole circles, he filtered his search, telling his skill to highlight only the traps that contained the specific rune sequence Samantha had identified.

A mental map lit up in his head.

“Okay… there are about this many around the main approach…”

Samantha’s eyes gleamed with excitement.

“In that case, if we just focus on disabling traps with that signature, can we clear a path along our expected route?”

Yoichi ran the simulation in his head.

“Hmm, it looks like we can narrow down the most dangerous ones quite a bit, yeah.”

“Excellent. Then, next…”

A triumphant grin could be seen spreading across Samantha’s face after that.

From there, their workflow transformed.

The tedious process of full-circle replication was thrown out the window.

Instead, Samantha would expertly draw a key component—a trigger sequence, a power conduit, an elemental sigil—and Yoichi would use his [Appraisal+] like a magical search engine, instantly listing all the traps along their path that contained that specific piece.

What had been a frustrating slog was quickly becoming an efficient, surgical operation.

The gloom in the workshop lifted, replaced by the buzz of productive energy. They had found their system.

Soon enough, the large map of Fallon, spread out across the workshop table, was starting to look like a madman’s diary.

It was covered in Yoichi’s notes on patrol routes, Karin’s markings for sniper nests, and now, a growing collection of arcane symbols sketched by Samantha.

She was meticulously drawing out the key geometric shapes she’d identified from the enemy’s magical landmines, creating a sort of “component library” of their trap designs.

For each shape Samantha drew, Yoichi cross-referenced it with his own observations, listing the specific magic circles he’d seen that contained those patterns.

Together, they were reverse-engineering the enemy’s defensive grid.

“How’s the master plan coming along?”

Yoichi asked, leaning over the map to get a better look.

Samantha tapped a section of the map where they’d marked a particularly dense cluster of traps.

“Pretty good. If we can compress the disabling signal to this extent, I think we’ll have a wide enough area of effect to clear a path.”

Karin also joined in, peering over Samantha’s shoulder.

“That’s a relief. Walking through there felt like trying to cross a snake pit blindfolded.”

“Exactly. Now for the fun part: breaking their toys.”

Samantha then pushed the map aside and grabbing a clean sheet of paper.

With a focused intensity, she began sketching, combining and inverting the patterns they had just analyzed.

Her pencil flew across the page, leaving a trail of intricate lines, curves, and runes.

She’d occasionally mutter to herself, scribble something out with a frustrated sigh, and start a new section.

After a few minutes of this feverish trial and error, a final, elegant magic circle took shape.

She then declared, holding it up with a triumphant grin.

“Yep, that should do it. This little beauty should be able to neutralize the most common types of magic circles they’re using.”

“Wow, you work ridiculously fast.”

Yoichi was genuinely impressed.

The entire process, from analyzing the enemy traps to designing a brand-new counter-measure, had taken her less than ten minutes.

Not only that, but she’d created a single circle that could disable multiple, distinct types of traps—a feat that would leave even a high-ranking court magician scratching their head.

“You studied programming back in your world, right, Yoichi?”

Samantha asked, tapping her new design.

“You see, magic circles here are a lot like that, if you just look at them the right way. It’s all about logic, inputs, and outputs. You just have to find the command that tells it to ‘turn off’.”

“Is that so…? It’s still amazing. Wait a second, how do _you_ know about programming?”

“Oh, I’ve learned the main languages. You know, the usual suspects. The learning materials Karin found for me were really good. Super easy to understand.”

She said casually as sipping coffee in a Monday morning.

Yoichi then turned to Karin, looking surprised.

“Karin, you were studying that stuff too?”

Karin gave a small, almost shy smile.

“Well, back in my old company, the girl in charge of web design was a total genius in that area. I consulted with her a bunch before I quit, and she gave me some great learning resources. I figured it might be useful, so I shared them with Samantha.”

“Really… So that’s what was going on.”

Yoichi was still a little stunned.

It seemed the women of their group were constantly sharing knowledge and skills without him even realizing it.

“We should try making one of the games from your world sometime!”

Samantha suggested excitedly.

“O-Okay, yeah, let’s definitely do that next time”

For a moment there, Yoichi’s mind briefly pictured a fantasy version of a retro game in the past.

As cool as that sounded, he forced himself to focus to the present events.

“For now, though, we need to clear Fallon.”

Samantha agreed, her focus snapping back instantly.

“Right, right. Mission first. Well then, I want to engrave this magic circle onto a projectile. I’m thinking a bullet… do you have any with flat warheads? A pointed tip might distort the pattern.”

“Good thinking. In that case, we can use flat-nosed ammunition. Would a standard 9mm work for you?” Yoichi asked, already reaching for his infinite storage.

“Yeah, that’s perfect.”

Yoichi materialized a single, brass-cased bullet and handed it to Samantha.

“Okay, now I just need to resize and encode this magic circle and…”

The alchemical blacksmith’s voice soon trailed off as she stared intently at the drawing in her hand, committing every line to memory.

She closed her eyes, her brow furrowing in concentration.

Then, she gently touched the flat, lead tip of the bullet with her index finger.

“Hmm, hmm… _Eii!_“

With a soft, almost cute little shout, a tiny pinprick of light flared to life in the gap between her fingertip and the bullet.

“And… there we go. I think this is about right”

When she’s done, she pulled her finger away.

Yoichi took the bullet and examined it.

Engraved on the flat tip, so small he almost needed to squint, was the perfect, miniature version of the magic circle she had just designed.

“Yeah, that’s incredible. Alright, let’s make about ten of these, just to be safe. What about arrows? We’ll need a ranged option that’s quieter than a gunshot.”

For an arrowhead, a hiraneflat-type would probably be best for the same reason,” Karin chimed in immediately.

“I’m on it!”

Before he could mutter a word, Samantha was already jogging towards the back of the workshop where they stored their smithing supplies.

“A ‘hirane’?” Yoichi repeated, stumbling over the word. “What’s that?”

Karin then explained patiently.

“It refers to the shape of the arrowhead. You know there are different types, right, Yoichi?”

“Well, I know the normal pointy ones, and those ‘whistling arrows’ you see in movies, the _kabura-ya_.”

A proud, teacher-like smile spread across Karin’s face.

“What you call ‘normal’ are _togari-ya_, or pointed arrows. And the head on a _kabura-ya_ or whistling arrows is actually a type of _karimata_, or ‘goose-foot’ arrowhead.”<sup>1</sup>

“You mean those ones shaped like a forked pole, the _sasumata_?”<sup>2</sup>

“Exactly! The inner edges of the fork are sharpened blades. It’s designed to cut and snag rather than just pierce,” Karin said, warming to her subject. “The _hirane_ is also designed to cut, but it looks more like…”

“How about this one?”

Samantha’s voice cut in as she returned, holding up a freshly forged arrowhead in a pair of tongs.

It looked like a miniature, spade-shaped sword tip—wide, flat, and sharp.

Yoichi’s eyes lit up with understanding when he saw the object.

“I see. That big flat surface will make it much easier to engrave the magic circle.”

“Exacto. Still, think you came up with this so quickly, Karin. You’re pretty sharp.” Samantha also beamed.

Karin puffed out her chest with a confident smile.

“Hehe, what can I say? I’m an archer, through and through.”

She’d been practicing Kyudo—Japanese Archery—for years, so it made sense she’d have a deep well of knowledge to draw from.

Still, Yoichi couldn’t help but feel a little impressed.

He couldn’t imagine anyone using arrowheads like these for traditional target practice.

_(Karin’s really been working hard on all fronts, hasn’t she?)_ he thought.

As François’s apprentice and the team’s dedicated archer, she was clearly honing both her practical skills and her historical knowledge.

“In that case, let’s make ten arrows as well,” Yoichi decided. “We can do some trial runs and work out any bugs before the real thing.”

“Okay,” Samantha agreed.

“Sounds good,” said Karin.

After another flurry of quiet, focused work, they had a batch of ten enchanted bullets and ten enchanted arrows.

The three of them then headed outside into the training garden behind the workshop.

“Let’s set up a guinea pig… right about here,” Samantha said, stopping in a clear patch of dirt. Then,

“Eii!”

She knelt down and slammed her palm flat against the ground.

A faint blue light spread from her hand, searing the intricate lines of a magic circle directly into the soil.

Then, standing up and dusting off her hands, she started to explain.

“This is a replica of the most common one we found. A pressure-and-proximity trap. It’s designed to erupt in a pillar of fire when you step on it or get too close.”

Yoichi nodded grimly.

“The kind that not only roasts you, but also acts as a giant ‘Hey, someone’s here!’ signal for the enemy.”

“Yeah, and they’re super annoying in the battlefield.”

“It certainly is a pain.”

Yoichi’s eyes narrowed. He activated his [Appraisal+] skill.

In his vision, glowing text and data overlaid the magical trap on the ground.

“Give it a once-over. Is the drawing accurate?”

“Yeah, looks like a perfect copy.”

Yoichi started confirming to Samantha, reading the details from his skill.

“[Fire Pillar Trap – Common Grade]. Activation by mana signature or physical pressure. Detection radius is about a meter. It seems to work without any problems… or, it _would_ work if we let it.”

Samantha started stepping back.

“Then, it’s showtime. Yoichi, if you would do the honors.”

“Okay.”

Yoichi drew the pistol from his holster, the enchanted bullet already chambered.

The familiar weight felt reassuring in his hand.

He took a steadying breath, lined up his sights on the very center of the magic circle etched into the ground, and squeezed the trigger.

――_Bang!_

The sharp crack of the gunshot echoed across the quiet garden as the bullet kicked up a puff of dirt right in the heart of the circle.

For a split second, nothing happened.

Then, the lines of the magic circle began to pulse with a faint, sickly green light.

“…Well? How’s it looking?” Samantha asked, leaning forward with anticipation.

As she spoke, the light sputtered and died.

The once-perfectly etched lines on the ground now looked corrupted, with thin, spidery cracks spreading out from the bullet hole like insect damage.

The magical energy that had been humming from it just moments before was completely gone.

“Yeah, looks we defused it,” Yoichi confirmed, lowering the pistol with a low whistle. “Completely nullified.”

“Hehe, of course it is!”

Samantha burst into a grin, placing her hands on her hips with a look of pure satisfaction.

The success of her anti-magic ammunition was a huge step forward.

“But one test isn’t enough data. Let’s not get ahead of ourselves.”

“My turn, then,” Karin said, stepping forward with her bow already in hand. “If this works for arrows too, then we’ll have a silent option.”

“Sure thing, Karin,” Samantha said, gesturing to another prepared magic circle landmine. “Let’s see what you’ve got.”

Karin nocked an arrow, its arrowhead glinting with the same faint runes as Yoichi’s bullets.

Unlike the explosive crack of the pistol, her draw was silent and fluid.

The bowstring twanged softly, and the arrow hissed through the air, embedding itself in its target with a solid _thwump_.

Just like with the bullet, the magic circle flared briefly before cracking and going dark.

They spent the next half-hour testing the rest of the prototypes, firing bullet after bullet and arrow after arrow.

Every single time, the result was the same: one shot was all it took to shatter the magic.

“Perfect! The concept is proven!” Samantha finally declared, clapping her hands together.

“Phase one is a success! Now for the hard part… mass production.”

---

“Whew… Alright, that’s the last one,” Samantha sighed, finally dropping her arms.

She stretched her back with a deep, satisfying groan, her whole body arching.

The workshop, which had been filled with the sharp scent of ozone and focused energy, now just felt hot and stuffy.

Her usual work attire of a simple tank top and shorts was plastered to her skin.

The thin fabric of her top, soaked clear through with sweat, clung tightly to her chest, outlining every curve and clearly showing the small bulge and raised bump in the center.

It had been a grueling few hours.

After getting the initial design for the bullets and arrowheads sorted, she had personally etched a total of 300 magic circles onto the tiny surfaces—a task requiring immense focus and magical stamina.

“Thanks for the help, Karin.”

Samantha turned to her friend with a grateful smile.

“You’re welcome.”

Karin replied, mirroring the stretch.

She was in a similar state, dressed in a simple blouse and panties, her own clothes darkened with perspiration.

Karin, with her exceptional talent for manipulating internal magical power, had been Samantha’s lifeline during the whole process.

Carving magic circles with Samantha’s unique method looked deceptively simple.

She would just point her finger, and a glowing line would sear itself into the target material.

But this “instant etch” technique was a brute-force method; it skipped all the careful, delicate steps of the process, which meant it chewed through her magical power at an alarming rate.

Even with her [Healthy Body βbeta] skill giving her what seemed like an endless supply of stamina and mana, there was a hard limit to how much she could output at once.

Normally, she’d have to stop for a good five or six-minute break after every ten etchings just to let her internal circuits cool down.

That’s where Karin came in.

“Honestly, thanks to you, Karin, I feel like we finished this in half the time.”

By placing her hands on Samantha’s back and skillfully guiding the flow of mana through her body, Karin acted like a human regulator, making the entire process vastly more efficient.

With her help, Samantha could power through fifteen etchings before needing a much shorter two or three-minute break.

“I’m just glad I could help,” Karin said, her breathing still a little heavy.

Her face was flushed, and she wiped a bead of sweat from her temple.

Manipulating someone else’s mana circulation was an incredibly draining task in its own right, requiring just as much concentration as Samantha’s etching.

On top of that, they had to maintain physical contact the entire time.

The sheer body heat radiating from Samantha as she burned through her magic was a significant factor.

Karin, who had started the work session in a casual blouse and tracksuit pants, had shed them for underwear within minutes.

A little while after that, feeling constricted and short of breath from the effort, she’d discreetly slipped off her bra as well.

“Aah… I’m just… completely drenched,” Karin murmured, fanning her face with her hand.

Her sweat-soaked shirt now clung to her body like a second skin, leaving absolutely nothing to the imagination about the prominent, hardened shape of her nipples and the full curve of her breasts beneath.

“Hey… you two really worked hard.”

Then, Yoichi’s voice came out, though a little strained.

He tried to sound encouraging, but it was hard not to be a bit embarrassed by the sight in front of him.

He’d seen them in various states of disarray more times than he could count, but the combination of their exhaustion and raw, unguarded femininity still managed to kick-start a familiar warmth in his gut.

“Nfufu… you have no idea, Yoichi. That was _really_ tiring,” Samantha purred, leaning against a workbench.

While Samantha and Karin had been pouring their life force into the magical enchanting, Yoichi had been handling the more mundane, yet equally vital, assembly.

Using the maintenance function of his [Infinite Storage+], he’d been loading the newly-enchanted bullets into magazines and fletching and fitting the magic arrowheads onto their shafts.

“Yeah, yeah, I know. I mostly just watched from the sidelines,” he said with a self-deprecating shrug.

Samantha shot him back with some motivation.

“Don’t sell yourself short. You saved me a ton of time. Fletching all those arrows by hand would have been an absolute nightmare.”

From Yoichi’s perspective, it was a simple job—just store the components and concentrate vaguely on the finished product.

But for them, it meant skipping hours of tedious, manual labor.

## Translator Notes:

1. The kabura-yawhistling arrows. togari-yapointed arrows, hiraneflat-type and karimatagoose-foot. These first two are the kinds of arrows used in ancient Japan. The latter two refers to the arrowheads, primarily their shapes.

![](https://stabbingwithasyringe.home.blog/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/image.jpeg?w=624)

This is a Hirane (flat-type) arrowhead with design holes shaped like cherry blossoms.

![](https://stabbingwithasyringe.home.blog/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/image.jpg?w=624)

These are Kabura-ya (whistling arrows), one with a flat-type tip (hirane) and one with karimata (goose-foot tip). The “bulb” part is the whistle. This is usually fired as some kind of signaling device when enemies are spotted or when exchanging messages.

![](https://stabbingwithasyringe.home.blog/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/image-2.jpeg?w=624)

These are arrowheads from Kamakura period (1100s – 1300s) consisting of hirane, a huge hirane, and karimata tips

2. Sasumata. Literally translated as “spear fork,” it’s a polearm used by the samurai class and their retainers in feudal Japan. They are used in capture of suspected criminals alive and with minimal harm.

![](https://stabbingwithasyringe.home.blog/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/image-1.jpeg?w=280)

Ancient design of sasumata. Notice the spikes alongside the pole to prevent the person being arrested from grabbing the pole.

![](https://stabbingwithasyringe.home.blog/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/image-3.jpeg?w=394)

Modern sasumata being used in capturing suspected criminals. They are now more of a self-defense tool, and are used not only by the police but also schools in case of hooligan invasions and are more on the safer side, with aluminum base and the lack of spikes

## **Chapter 2 – In-charge of TOKOROTEN’s Rear 2 ※**

Methods to neutralize them had been more or less established, and with some on-site adjustments, they were confident they could clear a path.

Beyond the minefield stood the provincial capital’s main defenses: a wide, deep moat and towering city walls.

No matter how high their physical abilities were, even if they were enhanced with magic, leaping over such obstacles was simply impossible.

Worse still, the entire perimeter was a web of detection systems.

This means using any form of magic, sorcery, or magical tool would be like setting off a flare in the dead of night, instantly activating defense mechanisms that would either sound blaring alarms or intercept them with overwhelming force.

Time just wasn’t in their favor right now.

If they waited that long, the guards would likely discover the neutralized magic circle mines, and if that happens, they would lose the element of surprise.

If they need to infiltrate the capital, and they needed to do it quickly and stealthily.

They were hardly any trouble. I slowly approached and snapped their necks.

The last one, even after the other two collapsed, didn’t notice—he was too absorbed in Spider-Man.

Researchers, it seemed, could become so fixated on what was before them that they ignored their surroundings.

Perhaps it was the same in both science and magic—I recalled that madman I had seen in the dream.

And so, I successfully secured Spider-Man’s corpse.

Up to this point, things were proceeding smoothly.

I was about to carry it away when I realized something as I drew closer.

(…So it only looked intact because it had been repaired. And this smell beneath the reek of chemicals…)

The flesh had completely rotted.

They had simply made it look presentable, using chemicals to suppress the stench.

“To think you’d tell me to eat this,” I muttered, even I hesitating for a moment.

But survival left me no choice.

I had to move it to a safe place first—but I had no memory of such a place nearby.

(At worst, into the forest of the former Empire. No way I’m taking this back to my base. It’s revolting, and it stinks. The problem is… how to carry it.)

Looking around the room, the solution quickly caught my eye.

The table on which Spider-Man lay—I could just carry that whole.

So I lifted the table.

If I had rope, I could secure the body, but unfortunately, I had none.

Carefully, I made my way through the cave, making sure the corpse didn’t fall, and stepped outside—

Only to find no ambush of soldiers waiting to see the carnage.

I slipped away easily.

It was almost anticlimactic.

I retrieved my backpack, and so far everything was nearly ideal—but I couldn’t lower my guard.

Avoiding human eyes, I headed south, carefully carrying the table through the forest.

After some time walking with the corpse, the sun was already past its zenith by the time I judged I had crossed into the former Empire’s lands.

“At least now I can breathe easier.”

I muttered this as I set down the table, pulled out a water tank from my pack, and drank.

The fruit I had been nibbling on was now gone, so I would soon need to procure food—but for the moment I was transporting not fresh meat, but rotting flesh.

I couldn’t risk leaving it unattended, lest wild animals feast on it.

While considering food, I looked at the corpse again.

“So this is what I have to eat…”

I poked it with my finger.

“…It squished.”

Undeniably rotten meat.

The thought made my resolve waver, and I found myself muttering again,

“You really want me to eat this?”

The longer time passed, the more my determination seemed to slip.

(No, that can’t be. I can do this—my teacher said I was capable. Eating some rotten meat is nothing.)

Still, one concern gnawed at me.

Ordinarily, eating rotten food meant stomach trouble.

But what about me?

Would my body absorb even things it shouldn’t?

The more I thought, the more uneasy I grew.

“…I’ll just try a little. Just a nibble.”

If it triggered the phenomenon, I could leave the rest to fate.

This area was still close enough to human lands, and thanks to my goblin-clearing, there were many wild animals but few monsters.

Even if I collapsed, nothing too threatening should be around.

I took a deep breath, steeling myself, and reached for Spider-Man’s corpse.

The squishy feel of the flesh made me grimace as I opened my mouth—then remembered.

Last time, when I had taken a finger into my mouth, I had chewed and swallowed naturally, without conscious intent.

Maybe this time too, if I put fingers in my mouth, my body would act on its own.

I tore off two fingers, closed my eyes, and tossed them in.

Nothing happened.

So I touched the cut ends with my tongue—

And vomited.

The putrid stench, the chemicals, and my body’s rejection of rotten flesh overwhelmed me, and I retched it all out.

But I wasn’t so weak as to give up here.

I grabbed the fallen fingers, shoved them back into my mouth, and chewed.

The result—no reaction.

I waited, but my body remained unchanged.

Unable to force down more, I spat them out, rinsed my mouth with water, and sighed.

I stared at the corpse.

“Too much time passed? Or maybe corpses don’t work? Or is it because they doused it in chemicals?”

I didn’t know.

But I had a strong sense it wouldn’t work.

(Wait… maybe that’s it!)

That scientist had said:

“This is a message for those who keep devouring rampaging subjects.”

So it was meant for eating the living.

This corpse—and even the failures in the facility—were likely outside the condition.

Maybe it was the spider half that needed eating, but since I couldn’t find it, that too was impossible.

If I’d realized sooner, I wouldn’t have wasted this effort.

Still, it was good I hadn’t asked the elves for help yet.

In the end, though the matter had reset, at least I had eliminated the nightmare of Spider-Man’s corpse being reused.

So overall, the outcome was positive.

Yes—nothing had been wasted.

Now, what to do with this inconvenient body?

After some thought, I concluded: “It’s just the human half—just leave it.”

“Yeah, it just looks like a half-eaten human.”

Anyone would think it was someone attacked by a monster, half-devoured, and abandoned.

So I would leave it to decompose naturally, deeper in the forest.

The table was wooden—I could smash it apart.

There were no human signs near the cave, and no survivors.

No way to link this to me.

Once I disposed of it, only a mystery would remain.

So, I set off to finish the job, carrying the corpse deeper into the woods.

It felt like covering up a crime.

Would Canaan’s great detectives solve it?

(Though maybe they don’t even have detectives. Well, good luck finding the culprit!)

In high spirits, I swung the table and flung the corpse into the forest.

The table smashed against a tree.

Too lazy to go further, I tore off what remained of the hand and scattered it on the ground.

“And that’s that!”

I declared, hands on my hips.

The problem was, my lifespan as a human had not advanced an inch.

I looked up at the sky, but only saw clear blue.

Soon, it would be dusk.

Standing here wouldn’t help, so since I had come this far, I might as well stop by the nearest town.

Not for requests—just to find something as a return gift for the fruit.

And since my base had started receiving visitors, I needed more dishes.

I might even find other useful items.

My next destination was decided.

As long as I had tasks, my mind stayed steady.

If I kept shaping circumstances where my human reason could persist, maybe—just maybe—I could manage.

+++

# **95**

Q. What do you think I should do to avoid becoming a monster in both body and mind?

A. The hell are you talking about?

My worries would surely have been handled like that back in Imperial days.

Feeling nostalgic for that era, I arrived at the ruined city of Eilqueel and, without fuss, went straight to the spot I had used as a bed last time, brushed off the dust, and immediately set about sleeping preparations.

It was night—couldn’t be helped.

I sensed goblins in the city, but if I shut the entrance it should be fine.

I doubted any idiot would mess with me, and even if they did, it would wake me up—I should be okay.

‘Today I’m beat,’ I thought, flopping onto my same old DIY cot, closing my eyes, and waiting for my consciousness to drop.

By the time I noticed, it was morning.

Sure enough, after long hours of activity, I slept like a log.

Now then, I wanted to put something solid in my stomach, but first I would give the city a quick cleanup.

This time I would leave a few goblins alive so they learned that living here meant getting killed.

I wasn’t sure goblins could learn, but I visited irregularly and slaughtered them often enough that they might remember.

So, before breakfast, I culled about fifty.

I didn’t think it had even been two months since my last visit, but these things really sprouted back fast.

After that, I went into the forest, brought down a hog, returned, butchered it, and started making breakfast.

As I grilled meat on an iron plate, I looked around and thought, “What should I bring back this time?”

Nothing in particular caught my eye, so after finishing my meal on the cracked roadway, I started tidying up.
